class="firstHeading" lang="en">Eric Clapton</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n\n</p>\n<table class="infobox vcard plainlist" J. Cale">J. J. Cale</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ericclapton.com/">www<wbr />.ericclapton<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Eric Patrick Clapton</b>, <span class="noexcerpt" style="font-size:100;"><a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">CBE</a></span> (born <span class="nowrap">30 March</span> 1945), is an English <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Blues" title="Blues">blues</a> guitarist, singer, and songwriter. He is the only <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_inductees#Multiple_inductees" title="List of Rock and Roll Hall of Fame inductees">three-time inductee</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>: once as a solo artist and separately as a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds" title="The Yardbirds">the Yardbirds</a> and of <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream</a>. Clapton has been referred to as one of the most important and influential guitarists of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-AST_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AST-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Clapton <a href="/wiki/List_of_guitarists_considered_the_greatest" class="mw-redirect" title="List of guitarists considered the greatest">ranked second</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine\'s list of the "<a href="/wiki/Top_100_Greatest_Guitar_Players_of_all_Time" class="mw-redirect" title="Top 100 Greatest Guitar Players of all Time">100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time</a>"<sup id="cite_ref-RS_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and fourth in <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibson Guitar Corporation">Gibson\'s</a> "Top 50 Guitarists of All Time".<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He was also named number five in <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine\'s list of "The 10 Best Electric Guitar Players" in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-Tyrangiel-Time2009-08-14_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tyrangiel-Time2009-08-14-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the mid-1960s Clapton left the Yardbirds to play with <a href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers" title="John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers">John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers</a>. Immediately after leaving Mayall, Clapton formed the <a href="/wiki/Power_trio" title="Power trio">power trio</a> Cream with drummer <a href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker" title="Ginger Baker">Ginger Baker</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce" title="Jack Bruce">Jack Bruce</a>, in which Clapton played sustained blues improvisations and "arty, blues-based psychedelic pop".<sup id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> After Cream broke up, he formed blues rock band <a href="/wiki/Blind_Faith" title="Blind Faith">Blind Faith</a> with Baker, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ric_Grech" title="Ric Grech">Ric Grech</a>.  Clapton\'s solo career began in the 1970s, where his work bore the influence of the mellow style of <a href="/wiki/J._J._Cale" title="J. J. Cale">J. J. Cale</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Marley" title="Bob Marley">Bob Marley</a>. His version of Marley\'s "<a href="/wiki/I_Shot_the_Sheriff" title="I Shot the Sheriff">I Shot the Sheriff</a>" helped reggae reach a mass market.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Two of his most popular recordings were "<a href="/wiki/Layla" title="Layla">Layla</a>", recorded with <a href="/wiki/Derek_and_the_Dominos" title="Derek and the Dominos">Derek and the Dominos</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson" title="Robert Johnson">Robert Johnson</a>\'s "<a href="/wiki/Cross_Road_Blues" title="Cross Road Blues">Crossroads</a>", recorded with Cream. Following the death of his son Conor in 1991, Clapton\'s grief was expressed in the song "<a href="/wiki/Tears_in_Heaven" title="Tears in Heaven">Tears in Heaven</a>", which was featured on his <i><a href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Unplugged (Eric Clapton album)">Unplugged</a></i> album.\n</p><p>Clapton has been the recipient of 18 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Award</a> for Outstanding Contribution to Music. In 2004 he was awarded a <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">CBE</a> at Buckingham Palace for services to music.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Brits_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brits-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He has received four <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Awards" title="Ivor Novello Awards">Ivor Novello Awards</a> from the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a>, including the Lifetime Achievement Award. In his solo career, Clapton has sold more than 130 million records worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1998, Clapton, a recovering alcoholic and <a href="/wiki/Drug_addiction" class="mw-redirect" title="Drug addiction">drug addict</a>, founded the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre" title="Crossroads Centre">Crossroads Centre</a> on <a href="/wiki/Antigua" title="Antigua">Antigua</a>, a medical facility for recovering substance abusers.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Influences"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Influences</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Legacy"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Legacy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Guitars"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Guitars</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Other_media_appearances"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Other media appearances</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Personal_life"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Personal life</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Relationships_and_children"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Relationships and children</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Political_views"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Political views</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Controversy_over_remarks_on_immigration"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Controversy over remarks on immigration</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#Wealth_and_assets"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Wealth and assets</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-23"><a href="#Car_collection"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Car collection</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-24"><a href="#Charitable_work"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Charitable work</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Football"><span class="tocnumber">7.7</span> <span class="toctext">Football</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-26"><a href="#Awards_and_honours"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Awards and honours</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-27"><a href="#Clapton&#39;s_music_in_film_and_TV"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Clapton\'s music in film and TV</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Discography"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Discography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Solo_studio_albums"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Solo studio albums</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-30"><a href="#Collaborations"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Collaborations</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-33"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>\n<p>Clapton was born on 30 March 1945 in <a href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey" title="Ripley, Surrey">Ripley, Surrey</a>, England, to 16-year-old Patricia Molly Clapton (<span class="nowrap">7 January</span> 1929 \xe2\x80\x93 March 1999) and Edward Walter Fryer (<span class="nowrap">21 March</span> 1920 \xe2\x80\x93 <span class="nowrap">15 May</span> 1985), a 25-year-old soldier from <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, Quebec.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Fryer shipped off to war prior to Clapton\'s birth and then returned to Canada. Clapton grew up believing that his grandmother, Rose, and her second husband, Jack Clapp, Patricia\'s stepfather, were his parents, and that his mother was actually his older sister. The similarity in surnames gave rise to the erroneous belief that Clapton\'s real surname is Clapp (Reginald Cecil Clapton was the name of Rose\'s first husband, Eric Clapton\'s maternal grandfather).<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Years later, his mother married another Canadian soldier and moved to Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-CND_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CND-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> leaving young Eric with his grandparents in <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GUI_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton received an acoustic <a href="/wiki/Hoyer_guitars" class="mw-redirect" title="Hoyer guitars">Hoyer guitar</a>, made in Germany, for his thirteenth birthday, but the inexpensive steel-stringed instrument was difficult to play and he briefly lost interest.<sup id="cite_ref-GUI_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Two years later Clapton picked it up again and started playing consistently.<sup id="cite_ref-GUI_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GUI-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Clapton was influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Blues_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Blues music">blues</a> from an early age, and practised long hours to learn the <a href="/wiki/Chord_(music)" title="Chord (music)">chords</a> of blues music by playing along to the records.<sup id="cite_ref-clap_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clap-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He preserved his practice sessions using his portable <a href="/wiki/Grundig" title="Grundig">Grundig</a> reel-to-reel tape recorder, listening to them over and over until he felt he\'d got it right.<sup id="cite_ref-clap_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clap-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thomp_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomp-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1961, after leaving <a href="/wiki/Hollyfield_School" title="Hollyfield School">Hollyfield School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Surbiton" title="Surbiton">Surbiton</a>, Clapton studied at the <a href="/wiki/Kingston_University" title="Kingston University">Kingston College of Art</a> but was dismissed at the end of the academic year because his focus remained on music rather than art. His guitar playing was so advanced that, by the age of 16, he was getting noticed.<sup id="cite_ref-thomp_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomp-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Around this time, Clapton began <a href="/wiki/Busking" class="mw-redirect" title="Busking">busking</a> around <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Thames" title="Kingston upon Thames">Kingston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">Richmond</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/West_End_of_London" title="West End of London">West End</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 1962, Clapton started performing as a duo with fellow blues enthusiast <a href="/wiki/Dave_Brock" title="Dave Brock">David Brock</a> in pubs around Surrey.<sup id="cite_ref-thomp_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thomp-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> When he was seventeen years old, Clapton joined his first band, an early British <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> group, the Roosters, whose other guitarist was <a href="/wiki/Tom_McGuinness_(musician)" title="Tom McGuinness (musician)">Tom McGuinness</a>. He stayed with this band from January until August 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In October of that year, Clapton did a seven-<a href="/wiki/Gig_(musical_performance)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gig (musical performance)">gig</a> stint with <a href="/wiki/Brian_Casser" title="Brian Casser">Casey Jones &amp; the Engineers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Early_career.2C_breakthrough.2C_and_international_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career,_breakthrough,_and_international_success">Early career, breakthrough, and international success</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Yardbirds_and_the_Bluesbreakers">The Yardbirds and the Bluesbreakers</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds" title="The Yardbirds">The Yardbirds</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers" title="John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers">John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers</a></div>\n<p>In October 1963, Clapton joined the Yardbirds, a blues-influenced <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> band, and stayed with them until March 1965. Synthesising influences from <a href="/wiki/Chicago_blues" title="Chicago blues">Chicago blues</a> and leading blues guitarists such as <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freddie_King" title="Freddie King">Freddie King</a>, and <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a>, Clapton forged a distinctive style and rapidly became one of the most talked-about guitarists in the British music scene.<sup id="cite_ref-unuhsh_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unuhsh-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The band initially played <a href="/wiki/Chess_Records" title="Chess Records">Chess</a>/<a href="/wiki/Checker_Records" title="Checker Records">Checker</a>/<a href="/wiki/Vee-Jay_Records" title="Vee-Jay Records">Vee-Jay</a> blues numbers and began to attract a large <a href="/wiki/Cult_following" title="Cult following">cult following</a> when they took over the <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Stones">Rolling Stones</a>\' residency at the <a href="/wiki/Crawdaddy_Club" title="Crawdaddy Club">Crawdaddy Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond,_London" title="Richmond, London">Richmond</a>. They toured England with American bluesman <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Boy_Williamson_II" title="Sonny Boy Williamson II">Sonny Boy Williamson II</a>; a joint LP album, recorded in December 1963, was issued in 1965.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG/210px-Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG" width="210" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG/315px-Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG/420px-Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Albert_Hall.001_-_London.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Appearing at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> in London for the first time in 1964, Clapton has since performed at the venue over 200 times.<sup id="cite_ref-Royal_Albert_Hall_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Royal_Albert_Hall-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Yardbirds\' rhythm guitarist, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Dreja" title="Chris Dreja">Chris Dreja</a>, recalled that whenever Clapton broke a guitar string during a concert, he would stay on stage and replace it. The English audiences would wait out the delay by doing what is called a "<a href="/wiki/Slow_clap" class="mw-redirect" title="Slow clap">slow handclap</a>". Clapton\'s nickname of "Slowhand" came from <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Gomelsky" title="Giorgio Gomelsky">Giorgio Gomelsky</a>, a pun on the slow handclapping that ensued when Clapton stopped playing while he replaced a string.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In December 1964, Clapton made his first appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, London, with the Yardbirds.<sup id="cite_ref-Royal_Albert_Hall_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Royal_Albert_Hall-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Clapton has performed at the Hall over 200 times, and has stated that performing at the venue is like "playing in my front room".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 1965, Clapton and the Yardbirds had their first major hit, "<a href="/wiki/For_Your_Love" title="For Your Love">For Your Love</a>", written by songwriter <a href="/wiki/Graham_Gouldman" title="Graham Gouldman">Graham Gouldman</a>, who also wrote hit songs for <a href="/wiki/Herman%27s_Hermits" title="Herman&#39;s Hermits">Herman\'s Hermits</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Hollies" title="The Hollies">the Hollies</a> (and would later achieve success of his own as a member of <a href="/wiki/10cc" title="10cc">10cc</a>). In part because of its success, the Yardbirds elected to move toward a pop-oriented sound, much to the annoyance of Clapton, who was devoted to the blues and not commercial success. He left the Yardbirds on the day that "For Your Love" went public, a move that left the band without its lead guitarist and most accomplished member. Clapton suggested fellow guitarist <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a> to be his replacement, but Page declined out of loyalty to Clapton,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> putting <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> forward.<sup id="cite_ref-unuhsh_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unuhsh-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\nBeck and Page played together in the Yardbirds for a while, but Beck, Page, and Clapton were never in the group together. They first appeared together on the 12-date benefit tour for Action for Research into <a href="/wiki/Multiple_sclerosis" title="Multiple sclerosis">multiple sclerosis</a> in 1983 with the first date taking place on 23 September at the Royal Albert Hall.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton joined <a href="/wiki/John_Mayall_%26_the_Bluesbreakers" title="John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers">John Mayall &amp; the Bluesbreakers</a> in April 1965, only to quit a few months later. In June, Clapton was invited to jam with <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">Jimmy Page</a>, recording a number of tracks that would be retroactively credited to <a href="/wiki/All-Stars_(band)" title="All-Stars (band)">The Immediate All-Stars</a>. In the summer of 1965 he left for Greece with a band called the Glands, which included his old friend Ben Palmer on piano. In November 1965 he rejoined John Mayall. In March 1966, while still a member of the Bluesbreakers, Clapton briefly collaborated on a <a href="/wiki/Side_project" title="Side project">side project</a> with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce" title="Jack Bruce">Jack Bruce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a> among others, recording only a few tracks under the name <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_and_the_Powerhouse" title="Eric Clapton and the Powerhouse">Eric Clapton and the Powerhouse</a>. During his second Bluesbreakers stint, Clapton gained a reputation as the best blues guitarist on the club circuit. Although Clapton gained world fame for his playing on the influential album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blues_Breakers_with_Eric_Clapton" title="Blues Breakers with Eric Clapton">Blues Breakers \xe2\x80\x93 John Mayall \xe2\x80\x93 With Eric Clapton</a></i>, this album was not released until he had left the band for the last time in July 1966.\n</p><p>Having swapped his <a href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster" title="Fender Telecaster">Fender Telecaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vox_AC30" title="Vox AC30">Vox AC30</a> amplifier for a 1960 <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul Standard</a> guitar and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplification" title="Marshall Amplification">Marshall amplifier</a>, Clapton\'s sound and playing inspired the famous <a href="/wiki/Slogan" title="Slogan">slogan</a> "<a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">Clapton is God</a>", spray-painted by an unknown admirer on a wall in <a href="/wiki/London_Borough_of_Islington" title="London Borough of Islington">Islington</a> in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\nThe <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> was captured in a now-famous photograph, in which a dog is urinating on the wall. Clapton is reported to have been embarrassed by the slogan, saying in his <i><a href="/wiki/The_South_Bank_Show" title="The South Bank Show">The South Bank Show</a></i> profile in 1987, "I never accepted that I was the greatest guitar player in the world. I always <i>wanted</i> to be the greatest guitar player in the world, but that\'s an ideal, and I accept it as an ideal".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Cream">Cream</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cream_(band)" title="Cream (band)">Cream (band)</a></div>\n<p>Clapton left the Bluesbreakers in July 1966 (replaced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Green_(musician)" title="Peter Green (musician)">Peter Green</a>) and was invited by drummer <a href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker" title="Ginger Baker">Ginger Baker</a> to play in his newly formed band Cream, one of the earliest <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(bands)" class="mw-redirect" title="Supergroup (bands)">supergroups</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Jack_Bruce" title="Jack Bruce">Jack Bruce</a> on bass (Bruce was previously of the Bluesbreakers, the <a href="/wiki/Graham_Bond" title="Graham Bond">Graham Bond Organisation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Mann" title="Manfred Mann">Manfred Mann</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Before the formation of Cream, Clapton was not well known in the United States; he left the Yardbirds before "For Your Love" hit the U.S. Top Ten, and had yet to perform there.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> During his time with Cream, Clapton began to develop as a singer, songwriter, and guitarist, though Bruce took most of the lead vocals and wrote the majority of the material with lyricist <a href="/wiki/Pete_Brown" title="Pete Brown">Pete Brown</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-unuhsh_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unuhsh-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Cream\'s first gig was an unofficial performance at the <a href="/wiki/Twisted_Wheel_Club" title="Twisted Wheel Club">Twisted Wheel Club</a> in Manchester on <span class="nowrap">29 July</span> 1966 before their full debut two nights later at the <a href="/wiki/National_Jazz_and_Blues_Festival" title="National Jazz and Blues Festival">National Jazz and Blues Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor</a>. Cream established its enduring legend with the high-volume blues jamming and extended solos of their live shows.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg/220px-Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg/330px-Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg/440px-Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg 2x" data-file-width="928" data-file-height="615" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cream_Clapton_Bruce_Baker_1960s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton (right) with Cream</div></div></div>\n<p>By early 1967, fans of the emerging blues-rock sound in Britain had begun to portray Clapton as Britain\'s top guitarist; however, he found himself rivalled by the emergence of <a href="/wiki/Jimi_Hendrix" title="Jimi Hendrix">Jimi Hendrix</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Acid_rock" title="Acid rock">acid rock</a>-infused guitarist who used wailing <a href="/wiki/Audio_feedback" title="Audio feedback">feedback</a> and <a href="/wiki/Effects_unit" title="Effects unit">effects pedals</a> to create new sounds for the instrument.<sup id="cite_ref-Jam_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Hendrix attended a performance of the newly formed Cream at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Westminster" title="University of Westminster">Central London Polytechnic</a> on <span class="nowrap">1 October</span> 1966, during which he sat in on a double-timed version of "<a href="/wiki/Killing_Floor_(Howlin%27_Wolf_song)" title="Killing Floor (Howlin&#39; Wolf song)">Killing Floor</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Jam_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jam-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Top UK stars, including Clapton, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a>, members of <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">the Rolling Stones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a>, avidly attended Hendrix\'s early club performances. Hendrix\'s arrival had an immediate and major effect on the next phase of Clapton\'s career.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton first visited the United States while touring with Cream. In March 1967, Cream performed a nine-show stand at the RKO Theater in New York. They recorded <i><a href="/wiki/Disraeli_Gears" title="Disraeli Gears">Disraeli Gears</a></i> in New York from 11 to 15 May 1967. Cream\'s repertoire varied from hard rock ("<a href="/wiki/I_Feel_Free" title="I Feel Free">I Feel Free</a>") to lengthy blues-based instrumental jams ("<a href="/wiki/Spoonful" title="Spoonful">Spoonful</a>"). <i>Disraeli Gears</i> featured Clapton\'s searing guitar lines, Bruce\'s soaring vocals and prominent, fluid bass playing, and Baker\'s powerful, polyrhythmic jazz-influenced drumming. Together, Cream\'s talents secured them as an influential <a href="/wiki/Power_trio" title="Power trio">power trio</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fool_guitar_(replica).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/140px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg" width="140" height="351" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/210px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg/280px-The_Fool_guitar_%28replica%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1169" data-file-height="2934" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fool_guitar_(replica).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Fool_(guitar)" title="The Fool (guitar)">The Fool guitar</a> <i>(replica shown)</i>, with its bright artwork and famous "woman tone", was symbolic of the 1960s psychedelic rock era.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 28 months, Cream had become a commercial success, selling millions of records and playing throughout the U.S. and Europe. They redefined the instrumentalist\'s role in rock and were one of the first blues-rock bands to emphasise musical virtuosity and lengthy jazz-style improvisation sessions. Their US hit singles include "<a href="/wiki/Sunshine_of_Your_Love" title="Sunshine of Your Love">Sunshine of Your Love</a>" (No.&#8239;5, 1968), "<a href="/wiki/White_Room" title="White Room">White Room</a>" (No.&#8239;6, 1968) and "<a href="/wiki/Crossroads_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossroads (song)">Crossroads</a>" (No.&#8239;28, 1969) \xe2\x80\x93 a live version of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Johnson (musician)">Robert Johnson\'s</a> "Cross Road Blues". Though Cream was hailed as one of the greatest groups of its day, and the adulation of Clapton as a guitar legend reached new heights, the <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> was short-lived. Drug and alcohol use escalated tension between the three members, and conflicts between Bruce and Baker eventually led to Cream\'s demise. A strongly critical <i>Rolling Stone</i> review of a concert of the group\'s second headlining U.S. tour was another significant factor in the trio\'s demise, and it affected Clapton profoundly.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cream\'s farewell album, <i><a href="/wiki/Goodbye_(Cream_album)" title="Goodbye (Cream album)">Goodbye</a></i>, featuring live performances recorded at <a href="/wiki/The_Forum_(Inglewood,_California)" title="The Forum (Inglewood, California)">The Forum</a>, Los Angeles, <span class="nowrap">19 October</span> 1968, was released shortly after Cream disbanded; it also featured the studio single "<a href="/wiki/Badge_(song)" title="Badge (song)">Badge</a>", co-written by Clapton and <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>. Clapton met Harrison and became close friends with him after the Beatles shared a bill with the Clapton-era Yardbirds at the <a href="/wiki/London_Palladium" title="London Palladium">London Palladium</a>. Clapton played the lead guitar solo on Harrison\'s "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>" from the Beatles\' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Beatles_(album)" title="The Beatles (album)">White Album</a></i> (1968). Harrison\'s debut solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/Wonderwall_Music" title="Wonderwall Music">Wonderwall Music</a></i>, in 1968, became the first of many Harrison solo records to include Clapton on guitar. Clapton would go largely uncredited for his contributions to Harrison\'s albums due to contractual restraints, and Harrison was credited as "L\'Angelo Misterioso" for his contributions to the song "Badge" on <i>Goodbye</i>. The pair would often play live together as each other\'s guest. A year after Harrison\'s death in 2001, Clapton was musical director for the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 1969, when the Beatles were recording/filming what became <i><a href="/wiki/Let_It_Be_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Let It Be (film)">Let It Be</a></i>, tensions became so acute that Harrison quit the group for several days, prompting the others to consider replacing him with Clapton, an idea that particularly appealed to <a href="/wiki/John_Lennon" title="John Lennon">John Lennon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Michael Lindsay-Hogg, television director of the recording sessions for <i>Let It Be</i>, states, "I was there when John mentioned Clapton \xe2\x80\x94 but that wasn\'t going to happen. Would Eric have become a Beatle? No. Paul didn\'t want to go there. He didn\'t want them to break up. Then George came back."<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Clapton was on good terms with all four of the Beatles; in December 1968 he had played with Lennon at <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones_Rock_and_Roll_Circus" title="The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus">The Rolling Stones Rock and Roll Circus</a></i> as part of the one-off group <a href="/wiki/The_Dirty_Mac" title="The Dirty Mac">the Dirty Mac</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cream briefly reunited in 1993 to perform at the ceremony inducting them into the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>; a full reunion took place in May 2005, with Clapton, Bruce, and Baker playing four sold-out concerts at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and three shows at New York\'s <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> that October.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Recordings from the London shows, <i><a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall_London_May_2-3-5-6,_2005" title="Royal Albert Hall London May 2-3-5-6, 2005">Royal Albert Hall London May 2-3-5-6, 2005</a></i>, were released on CD, LP, and DVD in September/December 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Blind_Faith.2C_Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Blind_Faith,_Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends">Blind Faith, Delaney and Bonnie and Friends</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Blind_Faith" title="Blind Faith">Blind Faith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaney and Bonnie and Friends">Delaney and Bonnie and Friends</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Blind_Faith_(1969).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg/220px-Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg/330px-Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg/440px-Blind_Faith_%281969%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="531" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Blind_Faith_(1969).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Blind Faith in 1969, with Clapton standing far right</div></div></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Eric_Clapton&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(July 2018)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Clapton\'s next group, <a href="/wiki/Blind_Faith" title="Blind Faith">Blind Faith</a> (1969), was composed of Cream drummer <a href="/wiki/Ginger_Baker" title="Ginger Baker">Ginger Baker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a> of <a href="/wiki/Traffic_(band)" title="Traffic (band)">Traffic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ric_Grech" title="Ric Grech">Ric Grech</a> of <a href="/wiki/Family_(band)" title="Family (band)">Family</a>, and yielded one LP and one arena-circuit tour. The <a href="/wiki/Supergroup_(music)" title="Supergroup (music)">supergroup</a> debuted before 100,000 fans in London\'s <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> on <span class="nowrap">7 June</span> 1969. They performed several dates in Scandinavia and began a sold-out American tour in July before their only album was released. The LP <i><a href="/wiki/Blind_Faith_(Blind_Faith_album)" title="Blind Faith (Blind Faith album)">Blind Faith</a></i> consisted of just six songs, one of them the hit "<a href="/wiki/Can%27t_Find_My_Way_Home" title="Can&#39;t Find My Way Home">Can\'t Find My Way Home</a>". The album\'s jacket image of a topless pubescent girl was deemed controversial in the US and was replaced by a photograph of the band. Blind Faith dissolved after less than seven months.\n</p><p>Clapton subsequently toured as a sideman for an act that had opened for Blind Faith, <a href="/wiki/Delaney_and_Bonnie_and_Friends" class="mw-redirect" title="Delaney and Bonnie and Friends">Delaney and Bonnie and Friends</a>. He also played two dates as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Plastic_Ono_Band" title="Plastic Ono Band">Plastic Ono Band</a> that autumn, including a recorded performance at the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Rock_and_Roll_Revival" title="Toronto Rock and Roll Revival">Toronto Rock and Roll Revival</a> in September 1969 released as the album <i><a href="/wiki/Live_Peace_in_Toronto_1969" title="Live Peace in Toronto 1969">Live Peace in Toronto 1969</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-lenn_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenn-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> On 30 September 1969, Clapton played lead guitar on Lennon\'s second solo single, "<a href="/wiki/Cold_Turkey" title="Cold Turkey">Cold Turkey</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 15 December 1969 Clapton performed with Lennon, George Harrison, and others as the Plastic Ono Band at a fundraiser for <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a> in London.<sup id="cite_ref-lenn_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lenn-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Delaney_Bramlett" title="Delaney Bramlett">Delaney Bramlett</a> encouraged Clapton in his singing and writing. Using the Bramletts\' backing group and an all-star cast of session players (including <a href="/wiki/Leon_Russell" title="Leon Russell">Leon Russell</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills" title="Stephen Stills">Stephen Stills</a>), Clapton recorded his first solo album during two brief tour hiatuses, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_(album)" title="Eric Clapton (album)">Eric Clapton</a></i>. Delaney Bramlett co-wrote six of the songs with Clapton, also producing the LP,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Bramlett" title="Bonnie Bramlett">Bonnie Bramlett</a> co-wrote "Let It Rain".<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The album yielded the unexpected US No.&#160;18 hit, <a href="/wiki/J._J._Cale" title="J. J. Cale">J. J. Cale</a>\'s "After Midnight". Clapton also worked with much of Delaney and Bonnie\'s band to record George Harrison\'s <i><a href="/wiki/All_Things_Must_Pass" title="All Things Must Pass">All Things Must Pass</a></i> in spring 1970.\n</p><p>During this busy season, Clapton also recorded with other artists including Dr. John, <a href="/wiki/Leon_Russell" title="Leon Russell">Leon Russell</a>, Plastic Ono Band, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Preston" title="Billy Preston">Billy Preston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ringo_Starr" title="Ringo Starr">Ringo Starr</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dave_Mason" title="Dave Mason">Dave Mason</a>. With Chicago blues artist <a href="/wiki/Howlin%27_Wolf" title="Howlin&#39; Wolf">Howlin\' Wolf</a>, he recorded <i><a href="/wiki/The_London_Howlin%27_Wolf_Sessions" title="The London Howlin&#39; Wolf Sessions">The London Howlin\' Wolf Sessions</a></i>, that also included long-time Wolf guitarist <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Sumlin" title="Hubert Sumlin">Hubert Sumlin</a> and members of the <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Stones">Rolling Stones</a>, Winwood, Starr, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-Koda_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koda-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  Despite the superstar line up, critic <a href="/wiki/Cub_Koda" title="Cub Koda">Cub Koda</a> noted: "Even Eric Clapton, who usually welcomes any chance to play with one of his idols, has criticized this album repeatedly in interviews, which speaks volumes in and of itself."<sup id="cite_ref-Koda_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Koda-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other noted recordings from this period include Clapton\'s guitar work on "Go Back Home" from <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills" title="Stephen Stills">Stephen Stills</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Stills_(album)" title="Stephen Stills (album)">self-titled first solo album</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22Layla.22_and_solo_career"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;Layla&quot;_and_solo_career">"Layla" and solo career</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Derek_and_the_Dominos">Derek and the Dominos</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Derek_and_the_Dominos" title="Derek and the Dominos">Derek and the Dominos</a></div>\n<p>With the intention of counteracting the "star" cult faction that had begun to form around him, Clapton assembled a new band composed of Delaney and Bonnie\'s former <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_section" title="Rhythm section">rhythm section</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Whitlock" title="Bobby Whitlock">Bobby Whitlock</a> as keyboardist and vocalist, <a href="/wiki/Carl_Radle" title="Carl Radle">Carl Radle</a> as the bassist, and drummer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Gordon_(musician)" title="Jim Gordon (musician)">Jim Gordon</a>, with Clapton playing guitar. It was his intention to show that he need not fill a starring role, and functioned well as a member of an ensemble.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> During this period, Clapton was increasingly influenced by <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">The Band</a> and their album <i><a href="/wiki/Music_from_Big_Pink" title="Music from Big Pink">Music from Big Pink</a></i>, saying, "What I appreciated about the Band was that they were more concerned with songs and singing. They would have three- and four-part harmonies, and the guitar was put back into perspective as being accompaniment. That suited me well, because I had gotten so tired of the virtuosity\xe2\x80\x94or <i>pseudo</i>-virtuosity\xe2\x80\x94thing of long, boring guitar solos just because they were expected. The Band brought things back into perspective. The priority was the song."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Derek_and_the_Dominos.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/220px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/330px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Derek_and_the_Dominos.png/440px-Derek_and_the_Dominos.png 2x" data-file-width="978" data-file-height="724" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Derek_and_the_Dominos.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton (right) with Derek and the Dominos</div></div></div>\n<p>The band was originally called "Eric Clapton and Friends". The name "Derek and the Dominos" was a fluke that occurred when the band\'s provisional name of "Del and the Dynamos" was misread as Derek and the Dominos.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Clapton\'s biography states that Tony Ashton of <a href="/wiki/Ashton,_Gardner_and_Dyke" title="Ashton, Gardner and Dyke">Ashton, Gardner and Dyke</a> told Clapton to call the band "Del and the Dominos", since "Del" was his nickname for Eric Clapton. Del and Eric were combined and the final name became "Derek and the Dominos".<sup id="cite_ref-nxfddy_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nxfddy-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton\'s close friendship with George Harrison brought him into contact with Harrison\'s wife, <a href="/wiki/Pattie_Boyd" title="Pattie Boyd">Pattie Boyd</a>, with whom he became deeply infatuated. When she spurned his advances, Clapton\'s unrequited affections prompted most of the material for the Dominos\' album, <i><a href="/wiki/Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs" title="Layla and Other Assorted Love Songs">Layla and Other Assorted Love Songs</a></i> (1970). Heavily blues-influenced, the album features the twin lead guitars of Clapton and Duane Allman, with Allman\'s <a href="/wiki/Slide_guitar" title="Slide guitar">slide guitar</a> as a key ingredient of the sound. Working at <a href="/wiki/Criteria_Studios" title="Criteria Studios">Criteria Studios</a> in Miami with <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic Records</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Tom_Dowd" title="Tom Dowd">Tom Dowd</a>, who had worked with Clapton on Cream\'s <i>Disraeli Gears</i>, the band recorded a double album.\n</p><p>The album features the hit love song "<a href="/wiki/Layla" title="Layla">Layla</a>", inspired by the classical poet of <a href="/wiki/Persian_literature" title="Persian literature">Persian literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nizami_Ganjavi" title="Nizami Ganjavi">Nizami Ganjavi</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Layla_and_Majnun" title="Layla and Majnun">The Story of Layla and Majnun</a></i>, a copy of which <a href="/wiki/Ian_Dallas" class="mw-redirect" title="Ian Dallas">Ian Dallas</a> had given to Clapton. The book moved Clapton profoundly, as it was the tale of a young man who fell hopelessly in love with a beautiful, unavailable woman and who went crazy because he could not marry her.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The two parts of "Layla" were recorded in separate sessions: the opening guitar section was recorded first, and for the second section, laid down a few weeks  later, drummer Jim Gordon played the piano part for the melody which he claimed to have written (though Bobby Whitlock stated that Rita Coolidge wrote it).<sup id="cite_ref-nxfddy_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nxfddy-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <i>Layla</i> LP was actually recorded by a five-piece version of the group, thanks to the unforeseen inclusion of guitarist <a href="/wiki/Duane_Allman" title="Duane Allman">Duane Allman</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Allman_Brothers_Band" title="The Allman Brothers Band">the Allman Brothers Band</a>. A few days into the Layla sessions, Dowd\xe2\x80\x94who was also producing the Allmans\xe2\x80\x94invited Clapton to an Allman Brothers outdoor concert in Miami. The two guitarists met first on stage, then played all night in the studio, and became friends. Duane first added his slide guitar to "<a href="/wiki/Tell_the_Truth_(song)" title="Tell the Truth (song)">Tell the Truth</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Nobody_Knows_You_When_You%27re_Down_and_Out" title="Nobody Knows You When You&#39;re Down and Out">Nobody Knows You When You\'re Down and Out</a>". In four days, the five-piece Dominos recorded "<a href="/wiki/Key_to_the_Highway" title="Key to the Highway">Key to the Highway</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Have_You_Ever_Loved_a_Woman" title="Have You Ever Loved a Woman">Have You Ever Loved a Woman</a>" (a <a href="/wiki/Blues_standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Blues standard">blues standard</a> popularised by <a href="/wiki/Freddie_King" title="Freddie King">Freddie King</a> and others), and "Why Does Love Got to be So Sad". In September, Duane briefly left the sessions for gigs with his own band, and the four-piece Dominos recorded "I Looked Away", "<a href="/wiki/Bell_Bottom_Blues_(Derek_and_the_Dominos_song)" title="Bell Bottom Blues (Derek and the Dominos song)">Bell Bottom Blues</a>", and "Keep on Growing". Duane returned to record "I am Yours", "<a href="/wiki/Anyday_(Derek_and_the_Dominos_song)" title="Anyday (Derek and the Dominos song)">Anyday</a>", and "It\'s Too Late". On 9 September, they recorded Hendrix\'s "<a href="/wiki/Little_Wing" title="Little Wing">Little Wing</a>" and the title track. The following day, the final track, "It\'s Too Late", was recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg/220px-Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg/330px-Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg/440px-Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2362" data-file-height="1898" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_%22slowhand%22_Clapton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eric Clapton in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, 1974</div></div></div>\n<p>Tragedy dogged the group throughout its brief career. During the sessions, Clapton was devastated by news of the death of Jimi Hendrix; eight days previously the band had cut a cover of "Little Wing" as a tribute to Hendrix. On <span class="nowrap">17 September</span> 1970, one day before Hendrix\'s death, Clapton had purchased a <a href="/wiki/Left-handedness" class="mw-redirect" title="Left-handedness">left-handed</a> <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a> that he had planned to give to Hendrix as a birthday gift. Adding to Clapton\'s woes, the <i>Layla</i> album received only lukewarm reviews upon release. The shaken group undertook a US tour without Allman, who had returned to the Allman Brothers Band. Despite Clapton\'s later admission that the tour took place amidst a veritable blizzard of drugs and alcohol, it resulted in the live double album <i><a href="/wiki/In_Concert_(Derek_and_the_Dominos_album)" title="In Concert (Derek and the Dominos album)">In Concert</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A second record was in the works when a clashing of egos took place and Clapton walked, thus disbanding the group. Allman was killed in a motorcycle accident on <span class="nowrap">29 October</span> 1971. Clapton wrote later in his autobiography that he and Allman were inseparable during the sessions in Florida; he talked about Allman as the "musical brother I\'d never had but wished I did".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Although Radle would remain Clapton\'s bass player until the summer of 1979 (Radle died in May 1980 from the effects of alcohol and narcotics), it would be 2003 before Clapton and Whitlock appeared together again (Clapton guested on Whitlock\'s appearance on the <i><a href="/wiki/Later_with_Jools_Holland" class="mw-redirect" title="Later with Jools Holland">Later with Jools Holland</a></i> show). Another tragic footnote to the Dominos story was the fate of drummer <a href="/wiki/Jim_Gordon_(musician)" title="Jim Gordon (musician)">Jim Gordon</a>, who was an undiagnosed <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenic</a> and years later murdered his mother during a <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychotic episode</a>. Gordon was confined to 16-years-to-life imprisonment, later being moved to a mental institution, where he remains today.<sup id="cite_ref-unuhsh_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unuhsh-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_problems_and_early_solo_success">Personal problems and early solo success</span></h4>\n<p>Clapton\'s career successes in the 1970s were in stark contrast with the struggles he coped with in his personal life, which was troubled by romantic longings and drug and alcohol addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> He became infatuated with <a href="/wiki/Pattie_Boyd" title="Pattie Boyd">Pattie Boyd</a>, who at the time was married to close friend <a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a>, and withdrew from recording and touring to isolation in his Surrey residence as the band broke up. There he nursed a <a href="/wiki/Substance_abuse" title="Substance abuse">heroin addiction</a>, which resulted in a lengthy career hiatus interrupted only by the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Bangladesh" class="mw-redirect" title="Concert for Bangladesh">Concert for Bangladesh</a> in August 1971 (where he passed out on stage, was revived, and managed to finish his performance).<sup id="cite_ref-unuhsh_19-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unuhsh-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> In January 1973, <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">the Who</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Pete_Townshend" title="Pete Townshend">Pete Townshend</a> organised a comeback concert for Clapton at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Theatre" title="Rainbow Theatre">Rainbow Theatre</a>, aptly titled the "<a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton%27s_Rainbow_Concert" title="Eric Clapton&#39;s Rainbow Concert">Rainbow Concert</a>", to help Clapton kick his addiction. Clapton returned the favour by playing "The Preacher" in <a href="/wiki/Tommy_(1975_film)" title="Tommy (1975 film)">Ken Russell\'s film version</a> of the Who\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_(rock_opera)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tommy (rock opera)">Tommy</a></i> in 1975; his appearance in the film (performing "Eyesight to the Blind") is notable as he is clearly wearing a fake beard in some shots, the result of deciding to shave off his real beard after the initial takes in an attempt to force the director to remove his earlier scene from the movie and leave the set.<sup id="cite_ref-nxfddy_49-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nxfddy-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg/220px-Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg/330px-Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg/440px-Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clapton_and_Elliman.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Elliman" title="Yvonne Elliman">Yvonne Elliman</a> with Clapton promoting <i><a href="/wiki/461_Ocean_Boulevard" title="461 Ocean Boulevard">461 Ocean Boulevard</a></i> in 1974</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1974, Clapton started living with Pattie Boyd (they would not marry until 1979) and was no longer using heroin (although he gradually began to drink heavily). He assembled a low-key touring band that included Radle, Miami guitarist <a href="/wiki/George_Terry_(musician)" title="George Terry (musician)">George Terry</a>, keyboardist Dick Sims (who died in 2011<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>), drummer <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Oldaker" title="Jamie Oldaker">Jamie Oldaker</a>, and vocalists <a href="/wiki/Yvonne_Elliman" title="Yvonne Elliman">Yvonne Elliman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcy_Levy" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcy Levy">Marcy Levy</a> (also known as Marcella Detroit). With this band Clapton recorded <i><a href="/wiki/461_Ocean_Boulevard" title="461 Ocean Boulevard">461 Ocean Boulevard</a></i> (1974), an album with an emphasis on more compact songs and fewer guitar solos; the cover version of "<a href="/wiki/I_Shot_the_Sheriff" title="I Shot the Sheriff">I Shot the Sheriff</a>" was Clapton\'s first number one hit and was important in bringing <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> and the music of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Marley" title="Bob Marley">Bob Marley</a> to a wider audience. The 1975 album <i><a href="/wiki/There%27s_One_in_Every_Crowd" title="There&#39;s One in Every Crowd">There\'s One in Every Crowd</a></i> continued this trend. The album\'s original title, <i>The World\'s Greatest Guitar Player (There\'s One in Every Crowd)</i>, was changed before pressing, as it was felt its ironic intention would be misunderstood. The band toured the world and subsequently released the 1975 live LP, <i><a href="/wiki/E._C._Was_Here" title="E. C. Was Here">E. C. Was Here</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Clapton continued to release albums and toured regularly. Highlights of the period include <i><a href="/wiki/No_Reason_to_Cry" title="No Reason to Cry">No Reason to Cry</a></i> (a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Band" title="The Band">The Band</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/Slowhand" title="Slowhand">Slowhand</a></i>, which featured "<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_Tonight" title="Wonderful Tonight">Wonderful Tonight</a>" and a second J. J. Cale cover, "<a href="/wiki/Cocaine_(song)" title="Cocaine (song)">Cocaine</a>". In 1976 he performed as one of a string of notable guests at the farewell performance of The Band, filmed in a <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> documentary called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Waltz" title="The Last Waltz">The Last Waltz</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Continued_success">Continued success</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAAEric_ClaptonTimepiecesTheBestOfEricClapton7xPlatinum.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/RIAAEric_ClaptonTimepiecesTheBestOfEricClapton7xPlatinum.jpg/220px-RIAAEric_ClaptonTimepiecesTheBestOfEricClapton7xPlatinum.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/RIAAEric_ClaptonTimepiecesTheBestOfEricClapton7xPlatinum.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="321" data-file-height="260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RIAAEric_ClaptonTimepiecesTheBestOfEricClapton7xPlatinum.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A seven-times Platinum <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a> certification for the album <i><a href="/wiki/Timepieces:_The_Best_of_Eric_Clapton" title="Timepieces: The Best of Eric Clapton">Timepieces: The Best of Eric Clapton</a></i> (1982)</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1981 Clapton was invited by producer <a href="/wiki/Martin_Lewis_(humorist)" title="Martin Lewis (humorist)">Martin Lewis</a> to appear at the <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> benefit <i><a href="/wiki/The_Secret_Policeman%27s_Other_Ball" title="The Secret Policeman&#39;s Other Ball">The Secret Policeman\'s Other Ball</a></i> in London. Clapton accepted the invitation and teamed up with Jeff Beck to perform a series of duets\xe2\x80\x94reportedly their first ever billed stage collaboration. Three of the performances were released on the album of the show, and one of the songs was featured in the film. The performances at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Drury_Lane_theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Drury Lane theatre">Drury Lane theatre</a> heralded a return to form and prominence for Clapton in the new decade. Many factors had influenced Clapton\'s comeback, including his "deepening commitment to Christianity", to which he had converted prior to his heroin addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-amg_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amg-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After calling his manager and admitting he was an alcoholic, Clapton flew to <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis%E2%80%93Saint_Paul" title="Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93Saint Paul">Minneapolis\xe2\x80\x93Saint Paul</a> in January 1982 and checked in at <a href="/wiki/Hazelden_Foundation" title="Hazelden Foundation">Hazelden Treatment Center</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Center_City,_Minnesota" title="Center City, Minnesota">Center City, Minnesota</a>. On the flight over, Clapton indulged in a large number of drinks, for fear he would never be able to drink again. Clapton wrote in his autobiography:<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>In the lowest moments of my life, the only reason I didn\'t commit suicide was that I knew I wouldn\'t be able to drink any more if I was dead. It was the only thing I thought was worth living for, and the idea that people were about to try and remove me from alcohol was so terrible that I drank and drank and drank, and they had to practically carry me into the clinic.\n</p></blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg/220px-TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg/330px-TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg/440px-TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1342" data-file-height="938" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:TinaTurner%26Clapton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> and Eric Clapton at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">Wembley Arena</a>, <span class="nowrap">18 June</span> 1987</div></div></div>\n<p>After being discharged, it was recommended by doctors of Hazelden that Clapton not partake in any activities that would act as triggers for his alcoholism or stress. A few months after his discharge, Clapton began working on his next album, against doctors\' orders. Working with Tom Dowd, he produced what he thought as his "most forced" album to date, <i><a href="/wiki/Money_and_Cigarettes" title="Money and Cigarettes">Money and Cigarettes</a></i>. Clapton chose the name of the album "because that\'s all I saw myself having left" after his first rehabilitation from alcoholism.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1984 he performed on former <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> member <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>\' solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking" title="The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking">The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking</a></i>, and joined the supporting tour. Since then Waters and Clapton have had a close relationship. In 2005 they performed together for the Tsunami Relief Fund. In 2006 they performed at the Highclere Castle, in aid of the Countryside Alliance, playing two set pieces of "<a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_song)" title="Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd song)">Wish You Were Here</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Comfortably_Numb" title="Comfortably Numb">Comfortably Numb</a>". Clapton, now a seasoned charity performer, played at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> concert on 13 July 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> When offered a slot close to peak viewing hours, he was apparently flattered. As Clapton recovered from his addictions, his album output continued in the 1980s, including two produced with <a href="/wiki/Phil_Collins" title="Phil Collins">Phil Collins</a>, 1985\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Behind_the_Sun_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Behind the Sun (Eric Clapton album)">Behind the Sun</a></i>, which produced the hits "Forever Man" and "She\'s Waiting", and 1986\'s <i><a href="/wiki/August_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="August (Eric Clapton album)">August</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg/220px-Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg/330px-Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg/440px-Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1412" data-file-height="1060" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harrison_and_Clapton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/George_Harrison" title="George Harrison">George Harrison</a> and Clapton at the <a href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince&#39;s Trust">Prince\'s Trust</a> Concert, Wembley Arena, London, 1987</div></div></div>\n<p><i>August</i> was suffused with Collins\'s trademark drum and horn sound, and became Clapton\'s biggest seller in the UK to date, matching his highest chart position, number 3. The album\'s first track, the hit "It\'s in the Way That You Use It", was featured in the <a href="/wiki/Tom_Cruise" title="Tom Cruise">Tom Cruise</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Paul_Newman" title="Paul Newman">Paul Newman</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Color_of_Money" title="The Color of Money">The Color of Money</a>.</i> The horn-peppered "Run" echoed Collins\' "<a href="/wiki/Sussudio" title="Sussudio">Sussudio</a>" and other work, while "Tearing Us Apart" (with <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a>) and "Miss You" continued Clapton\'s more angry sound. This rebound kicked off Clapton\'s two-year period of touring with Collins and their <i>August</i> collaborators, bassist <a href="/wiki/Nathan_East" title="Nathan East">Nathan East</a> and keyboard player/songwriter <a href="/wiki/Greg_Phillinganes" title="Greg Phillinganes">Greg Phillinganes</a>. While on tour for <i>August</i>, two concert videos were recorded of the four-man band, <i>Eric Clapton Live from Montreux</i> and <i>Eric Clapton and Friends</i>. Clapton later remade "After Midnight" as a single and a promotional track for the <a href="/wiki/Michelob" class="mw-redirect" title="Michelob">Michelob</a> beer brand, which had also used earlier songs by Collins and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a>. Clapton won a <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Television_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy Television Award">British Academy Television Award</a> for his collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen" title="Michael Kamen">Michael Kamen</a> on the score for the 1985 <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">BBC Television</a> thriller serial <i><a href="/wiki/Edge_of_Darkness" title="Edge of Darkness">Edge of Darkness</a></i>. In 1989, Clapton released <i><a href="/wiki/Journeyman_(album)" title="Journeyman (album)">Journeyman</a></i>, an album which covered a wide range of styles including blues, jazz, soul and pop. Collaborators included George Harrison, Phil Collins, <a href="/wiki/Daryl_Hall" title="Daryl Hall">Daryl Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chaka_Khan" title="Chaka Khan">Chaka Khan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mick_Jones_(Foreigner)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mick Jones (Foreigner)">Mick Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Sanborn" title="David Sanborn">David Sanborn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Cray" title="Robert Cray">Robert Cray</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/List_of_BRIT_Awards_ceremonies#1987" class="mw-redirect" title="List of BRIT Awards ceremonies">1987</a> <a href="/wiki/Brit_Awards" title="Brit Awards">Brit Awards</a> in London, Clapton was awarded the prize for Outstanding Contribution to Music.<sup id="cite_ref-Brits_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brits-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton would also get together with the <a href="/wiki/Bee_Gees" title="Bee Gees">Bee Gees</a> for charity. The supergroup called itself <a href="/wiki/The_Bunburys" class="mw-redirect" title="The Bunburys">The Bunburys</a>, and recorded a charity album with the proceeds going to the <a href="/wiki/Bunbury,_Cheshire" title="Bunbury, Cheshire">Bunbury Cricket Club</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a>, which plays exhibition cricket matches to raise money for nonprofit organisations in England. The Bunburys recorded three songs for <i>The Bunbury Tails</i>: "We\'re the Bunburys", "Bunbury Afternoon", and "Fight (No Matter How Long)". The last song also appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_1988_Summer_Olympics_Album" class="mw-redirect" title="The 1988 Summer Olympics Album">The 1988 Summer Olympics Album</a></i>, and went to No.&#8239;8 on the rock music chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Bunburys_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bunburys-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Clapton also played at the cricket club\'s 25th anniversary celebrations in 2011 which was held at London\'s Grosvenor House Hotel.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Tragedy.2C_healing_and_resurgence"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Tragedy,_healing_and_resurgence">Tragedy, healing and resurgence</span></h3>\n<p>The 1990s brought a series of 32 concerts to the Royal Albert Hall, such as the <a href="/wiki/24_Nights" title="24 Nights">24 Nights</a> series of concerts that took place around January through February 1990, and February to March 1991. On <span class="nowrap">27 August</span> 1990, fellow blues guitarist <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray_Vaughan" title="Stevie Ray Vaughan">Stevie Ray Vaughan</a>, who was touring with Clapton, and three members of their road crew were killed in a helicopter crash between concerts. Then, on <span class="nowrap">20 March</span> 1991, Clapton\'s four-year-old son, Conor, died after falling from the 53rd-floor window of his mother\'s friend\'s New York City apartment at 117 East 57th Street. Conor\'s funeral took place on 28 March at St Mary Magdalene\'s Church in Clapton\'s home village in <a href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey" title="Ripley, Surrey">Ripley, Surrey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:28%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">I almost subconsciously used music for myself as a healing agent, and lo and behold, it worked&#160;... I have got a great deal of happiness and a great deal of healing from music.</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Clapton on the healing process in writing "Tears in Heaven".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Clapton\'s grief was expressed in the song "<a href="/wiki/Tears_in_Heaven" title="Tears in Heaven">Tears in Heaven</a>", which was co-written by <a href="/wiki/Will_Jennings" title="Will Jennings">Will Jennings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/35th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="35th Annual Grammy Awards">35th Annual Grammy Awards</a>, Clapton received six <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Awards">Grammys</a> for the single "Tears in Heaven" and his <i><a href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Unplugged (Eric Clapton album)">Unplugged</a></i> album.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <i>Unplugged</i> features Clapton performing live in front of a small audience on 16 January 1992 at <a href="/wiki/Bray_Studios_(UK)" title="Bray Studios (UK)">Bray Film Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Berkshire" title="Windsor, Berkshire">Windsor, Berkshire</a>, England.
