The album reached number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, and is certified <a href="/wiki/Diamond_album" class="mw-redirect" title="Diamond album">Diamond</a> by the <a href="/wiki/RIAA" class="mw-redirect" title="RIAA">RIAA</a> for selling over 10 million copies in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> It reached number two in the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> and is certified four times platinum in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> On 9 September 1992, Clapton performed "Tears in Heaven" at the <a href="/wiki/1992_MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="1992 MTV Video Music Awards">1992 MTV Video Music Awards</a>, and won the award for Best Male Video.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 1992 he received the <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Novello_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Ivor Novello Award">Ivor Novello Award</a> for Lifetime Achievement from the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Songwriters,_Composers_and_Authors" class="mw-redirect" title="British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors">British Academy of Songwriters, Composers and Authors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 1992 Clapton was among the dozens of artists performing at <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">Bob Dylan</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/30th_Anniversary_Concert_Celebration" class="mw-redirect" title="30th Anniversary Concert Celebration">30th Anniversary Concert Celebration</a>. Recorded at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York City, the live two-disk CD/DVD captured a show full of celebrities performing classic Dylan songs, with Clapton playing the lead on a nearly 7-minute version of Dylan\'s "<a href="/wiki/Knockin%27_on_Heaven%27s_Door" title="Knockin&#39; on Heaven&#39;s Door">Knockin\' on Heaven\'s Door</a>" as part of the finale.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> While <i>Unplugged</i> featured Clapton playing <a href="/wiki/Steel-string_guitar" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel-string guitar">acoustic guitar</a>, his 1994 album <i><a href="/wiki/From_the_Cradle" title="From the Cradle">From the Cradle</a></i> contained new versions of old <a href="/wiki/Blues_standards" class="mw-redirect" title="Blues standards">blues standards</a>, highlighted by his electric guitar playing.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In 1995, Clapton for the first and only time featured on a UK No. 1 single, collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Chrissie_Hynde" title="Chrissie Hynde">Chrissie Hynde</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cher" title="Cher">Cher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neneh_Cherry" title="Neneh Cherry">Neneh Cherry</a> on a solo to a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Love_Can_Build_a_Bridge" title="Love Can Build a Bridge">Love Can Build a Bridge</a>" released in aid of the British charity telethon <a href="/wiki/Comic_Relief_(charity)" class="mw-redirect" title="Comic Relief (charity)">Comic Relief</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton\'s 1996 recording of the <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Kirkpatrick" title="Wayne Kirkpatrick">Wayne Kirkpatrick</a>/<a href="/wiki/Gordon_Kennedy_(musician)" title="Gordon Kennedy (musician)">Gordon Kennedy</a>/<a href="/wiki/Tommy_Sims" title="Tommy Sims">Tommy Sims</a> tune "Change the World" (featured in the soundtrack of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Phenomenon_(film)" title="Phenomenon (film)">Phenomenon</a></i>) won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Song_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Song of the Year">Grammy Award for Song of the Year</a> in 1997, the same year he recorded <i>Retail Therapy</i> (an album of <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> with <a href="/wiki/Simon_Climie" title="Simon Climie">Simon Climie</a> under the pseudonym <a href="/wiki/X-sample" class="mw-redirect" title="X-sample">TDF</a>).  On 15 September 1997, Clapton appeared at the <i><a href="/wiki/Music_for_Montserrat" title="Music for Montserrat">Music for Montserrat</a></i> concert at the Royal Albert Hall, London, performing "Layla" and "Same Old Blues" before finishing with "Hey Jude" alongside fellow English artists <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>, Phil Collins, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> That autumn, Clapton released the album <i><a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Pilgrim (Eric Clapton album)">Pilgrim</a></i>, the first record featuring new material for almost a decade.<sup id="cite_ref-amg_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-amg-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1996 Clapton had a relationship with singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a>. They remain friends, and Clapton appeared as a guest on Crow\'s Central Park Concert. The duo performed a Cream hit single, "<a href="/wiki/White_Room" title="White Room">White Room</a>". Later, Clapton and Crow performed an alternate version of "Tulsa Time" with other guitar legends at the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a> in June 2007 as well as <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson" title="Robert Johnson">Robert Johnson</a>\'s blues classic "<a href="/wiki/Cross_Road_Blues" title="Cross Road Blues">Crossroads</a>" at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> in August 2008 with <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Randolph_and_the_Family_Band" title="Robert Randolph and the Family Band">Robert Randolph</a>.\n</p><p>In 1998 Clapton, then 53, met 22-year-old administrative assistant Melia McEnery in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>, at a party given for him after a performance. He quietly dated her for a year, and went public with the relationship in 1999. They married on <span class="nowrap">1 January</span> 2001 at St Mary Magdalene church in Clapton\'s birthplace, <a href="/wiki/Ripley,_Surrey" title="Ripley, Surrey">Ripley</a>. They have three daughters, Julie Rose (<span class="nowrap">13 June</span> 2001), Ella May (<span class="nowrap">14 January</span> 2003), and Sophie Belle (<span class="nowrap">1 February</span> 2005).\n</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/41st_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="41st Annual Grammy Awards">41st Annual Grammy Awards</a> on 24 February 1999, Clapton received his third <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Male_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance">Grammy Award for Best Male Pop Vocal Performance</a>, for his song "My Father\'s Eyes".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> In October 1999, the compilation album, <i><a href="/wiki/Clapton_Chronicles:_The_Best_of_Eric_Clapton" title="Clapton Chronicles: The Best of Eric Clapton">Clapton Chronicles: The Best of Eric Clapton</a></i>, was released, which contained a new song, "<a href="/wiki/Blue_Eyes_Blue" title="Blue Eyes Blue">Blue Eyes Blue</a>", that also appears in soundtrack for the film, <i><a href="/wiki/Runaway_Bride_(film)" title="Runaway Bride (film)">Runaway Bride</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Clapton finished the twentieth century with collaborations with <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Santana" title="Carlos Santana">Carlos Santana</a> and <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaboration_albums">Collaboration albums</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eclapton_cardiff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Eclapton_cardiff.jpg/170px-Eclapton_cardiff.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Eclapton_cardiff.jpg/255px-Eclapton_cardiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Eclapton_cardiff.jpg/340px-Eclapton_cardiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1373" data-file-height="1830" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eclapton_cardiff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton performing for <a href="/wiki/Tsunami_Relief_Cardiff" title="Tsunami Relief Cardiff">Tsunami Relief Cardiff</a> at the Millennium Stadium in Cardiff, Wales on 22 January 2005</div></div></div>\n<p>Following the release of the 2001 record <i><a href="/wiki/Reptile_(album)" title="Reptile (album)">Reptile</a></i>, in June 2002, Clapton performed "Layla" and "While My Guitar Gently Weeps" at the <a href="/wiki/Party_at_the_Palace" title="Party at the Palace">Party at the Palace</a> concert in the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Buckingham_Palace" title="Buckingham Palace">Buckingham Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> On 29 November 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_George" title="Concert for George">Concert for George</a> was held at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>, a tribute to George Harrison, who had died a year earlier of lung cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-2002concert_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002concert-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Clapton was a performer and the musical director. The concert featured Paul McCartney, Ringo Starr, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Lynne" title="Jeff Lynne">Jeff Lynne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Petty_and_the_Heartbreakers" title="Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers">Tom Petty and the Heartbreakers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ravi_Shankar" title="Ravi Shankar">Ravi Shankar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Brooker" title="Gary Brooker">Gary Brooker</a>, Billy Preston, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Brown_(singer)" title="Joe Brown (singer)">Joe Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dhani_Harrison" title="Dhani Harrison">Dhani Harrison</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2002concert_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2002concert-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Clapton released two albums of covers of songs by bluesman <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Johnson (musician)">Robert Johnson</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Me_and_Mr._Johnson" title="Me and Mr. Johnson">Me and Mr. Johnson</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Me_and_Mr._Johnson#Sessions_for_Robert_J" title="Me and Mr. Johnson">Sessions for Robert J</a></i>.  Guitarist <a href="/wiki/Doyle_Bramhall_II" title="Doyle Bramhall II">Doyle Bramhall II</a> worked on the album with Clapton (after opening Clapton\'s 2001 tour with his band Smokestack) and would join him on his 2004 tour. In 2004, <i>Rolling Stone</i> ranked Clapton No.&#160;53 on their <a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone%27s_100_Greatest_Artists_of_All_Time" title="Rolling Stone&#39;s 100 Greatest Artists of All Time">list of the "100 Greatest Artists of All Time"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clapton2342.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Clapton2342.jpg/170px-Clapton2342.jpg" width="170" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Clapton2342.jpg/255px-Clapton2342.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Clapton2342.jpg/340px-Clapton2342.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="938" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clapton2342.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton performing at the <a href="/wiki/Ahoy_Rotterdam" title="Ahoy Rotterdam">Ahoy Arena</a> of Rotterdam on 1 June 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>On 22 January 2005, Clapton performed in the <a href="/wiki/Tsunami_Relief_Cardiff" title="Tsunami Relief Cardiff">Tsunami Relief Concert</a> held at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, in aid of the victims of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Indian_Ocean_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 Indian Ocean earthquake">2004 Indian Ocean earthquake</a>. In May 2005 Eric Clapton, Jack Bruce, and Ginger Baker reunited as Cream for a series of concerts at the Royal Albert Hall in London. Concert recordings were released on CD and DVD. Later, Cream performed in New York at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Back_Home_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Back Home (Eric Clapton album)">Back Home</a></i>, Clapton\'s first album of new original material in nearly five years, was released on <a href="/wiki/Reprise_Records" title="Reprise Records">Reprise Records</a> on <span class="nowrap">30 August</span>.\n</p><p>A collaboration with guitarist J. J. Cale, titled <i><a href="/wiki/The_Road_to_Escondido" title="The Road to Escondido">The Road to Escondido</a></i>, was released on <span class="nowrap">7 November</span> 2006, featuring <a href="/wiki/Derek_Trucks" title="Derek Trucks">Derek Trucks</a> and Billy Preston (Preston had also been a part of Clapton\'s 2004 touring band). The 14-track CD was produced and recorded by the duo in August 2005 in California. He invited Trucks to join his band for his 2006\xe2\x80\x932007 world tour.  Bramhall remained in the band as well, giving Clapton three elite guitarists in his band and thus allowing him to revisit many Derek and the Dominos songs that he hadn\'t played in decades. Trucks became the third member of the Allman Brothers Band to tour supporting Clapton, the second being pianist/keyboardist <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Leavell" title="Chuck Leavell">Chuck Leavell</a>, who appeared on the <i><a href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged" title="MTV Unplugged">MTV Unplugged</a></i> album and the <i><a href="/wiki/24_Nights" title="24 Nights">24 Nights</a></i> performances at the Royal Albert Hall, London in 1990 and 1991, as well as Clapton\'s 1992 US tour.<sup id="cite_ref-Music_Legends_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Music_Legends-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 May 2006, Clapton performed with <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">Queen</a> drummer <a href="/wiki/Roger_Meddows-Taylor" class="mw-redirect" title="Roger Meddows-Taylor">Roger Taylor</a> and former <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a> bassist/songwriter <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> at <a href="/wiki/Highclere_Castle" title="Highclere Castle">Highclere Castle</a>, Hampshire, in support of the <a href="/wiki/Countryside_Alliance" title="Countryside Alliance">Countryside Alliance</a> which promotes issues relating to the British countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On <span class="nowrap">13 August</span> 2006, Clapton made a guest appearance at the Bob Dylan concert in <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Ohio" title="Columbus, Ohio">Columbus, Ohio</a>, playing guitar on three songs in <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Vaughan" title="Jimmie Vaughan">Jimmie Vaughan</a>\'s opening act.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The chemistry between Trucks and Clapton convinced him to invite <a href="/wiki/The_Derek_Trucks_Band" title="The Derek Trucks Band">the Derek Trucks Band</a> to open for Clapton\'s set at his 2007 <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a>. Trucks remained on set afterward and performed with Clapton\'s band throughout his performances. The rights to Clapton\'s official memoirs, written by Christopher Simon Sykes and published in 2007, were sold at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Book_Fair" title="Frankfurt Book Fair">Frankfurt Book Fair</a> for <span class="nowrap">US$4 million</span>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 26 February 2008, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korean</a> officials had invited Clapton to play a concert in the <a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">communist state</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Clapton\'s management received the invitation and passed it on to the singer, who agreed in principle and suggested it take place sometime in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Kristen Foster, a spokesperson, said, "Eric Clapton receives numerous offers to play in countries around the world", and "[t]here is no agreement whatsoever for him to play in North Korea".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg/210px-CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg" width="210" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg/315px-CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg/420px-CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2285" data-file-height="2272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CrossroadsGuitarFestival2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton (left) and actor <a href="/wiki/Bill_Murray" title="Bill Murray">Bill Murray</a> kicking off the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a>, Illinois on 27 July 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007 Clapton learned more about his father, a Canadian soldier who left the UK after the war. Although Clapton\'s grandparents eventually told him the truth about his parentage, he only knew that his father\'s name was Edward Fryer. This was a source of disquiet for Clapton, as witnessed by his 1998 song "<a href="/wiki/My_Father%27s_Eyes_(song)" title="My Father&#39;s Eyes (song)">My Father\'s Eyes</a>". A <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> journalist named Michael Woloschuk researched Canadian Armed Forces service records and tracked down members of Fryer\'s family, and finally pieced together the story. He learned that Clapton\'s father was Edward Walter Fryer, born <span class="nowrap">21 March</span> 1920, in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a> and died <span class="nowrap">15 May 1985</span> in <a href="/wiki/Newmarket,_Ontario" title="Newmarket, Ontario">Newmarket, Ontario</a>. Fryer was a musician (piano and saxophone) and a lifelong drifter who was married several times, had several children, and apparently never knew that he was the father of Eric Clapton.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Clapton thanked Woloschuk in an encounter at Macdonald Cartier Airport, in Ottawa, Ontario, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2008 Clapton performed with his long-time friend <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a> at Madison Square Garden and guested on his recorded single, "Dirty City", on Winwood\'s album <i><a href="/wiki/Nine_Lives_(Steve_Winwood_album)" title="Nine Lives (Steve Winwood album)">Nine Lives</a></i>. The two former Blind Faith bandmates met again for a series of 14 concerts throughout the United States in June 2009. Clapton\'s 2008 Summer Tour began on <span class="nowrap">3 May</span> at the <a href="/wiki/Ford_Amphitheatre_(Tampa)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Amphitheatre (Tampa)">Ford Amphitheatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tampa,_Florida" title="Tampa, Florida">Tampa, Florida</a>, and then moved to Canada, Ireland, England, Norway, Iceland, Denmark, Poland, Germany, and Monaco. On <span class="nowrap">28 June</span> 2008, he headlined Saturday night for <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Calling" class="mw-redirect" title="Hard Rock Calling">Hard Rock Calling</a> 2008 in London\'s Hyde Park (previously Hyde Park Calling) with support from <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In September 2008 Clapton performed at a private charity fundraiser for The Countryside Alliance at Floridita in <a href="/wiki/Soho" title="Soho">Soho</a>, London, that included such guests as the London Mayor <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">Boris Johnson</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg/220px-Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg/330px-Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg/440px-Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2100" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Layla_and_Other_Assorted_Love_Songs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton (right) performing with <a href="/wiki/The_Allman_Brothers_Band" title="The Allman Brothers Band">the Allman Brothers Band</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Theatre_(New_York_City)" title="Beacon Theatre (New York City)">Beacon Theatre</a>, New York City in March 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>In March 2009, the Allman Brothers Band (amongst many notable guests) celebrated their 40th year, dedicating their string of concerts to the late Duane Allman on their annual run at the <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Theatre_(New_York_City)" title="Beacon Theatre (New York City)">Beacon Theatre</a>. Eric Clapton was one of the performers, with drummer <a href="/wiki/Butch_Trucks" title="Butch Trucks">Butch Trucks</a> remarking that the performance was not the typical Allman Brothers experience, given the number and musical styles of the guests who were invited to perform. Songs like "<a href="/wiki/In_Memory_of_Elizabeth_Reed" title="In Memory of Elizabeth Reed">In Memory of Elizabeth Reed</a>" were punctuated with others, including "<a href="/wiki/The_Weight" title="The Weight">The Weight</a>", with <a href="/wiki/Levon_Helm" title="Levon Helm">Levon Helm</a>; <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Winter" title="Johnny Winter">Johnny Winter</a> sitting in on Hendrix\'s "<a href="/wiki/Red_House_(song)" title="Red House (song)">Red House</a>"; and "Layla". On <span class="nowrap">4 May</span> 2009 Clapton appeared as a featured guest at the Royal Albert Hall, playing "<a href="/wiki/Further_on_Up_the_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="Further on Up the Road">Further on Up the Road</a>" with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Bonamassa" title="Joe Bonamassa">Joe Bonamassa</a>.\n</p><p>Clapton was scheduled to be one of the performers at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>\'s 25th anniversary concert in Madison Square Garden on <span class="nowrap">30 October</span> 2009, but cancelled due to <a href="/wiki/Gallstone" title="Gallstone">gallstone</a> surgery.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Van_Morrison" title="Van Morrison">Van Morrison</a> (who also cancelled)<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> said in an interview that he and Clapton were to do a "couple of songs", but that they would do something else together at "some other stage of the game".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Clapton.2C_Old_Sock_and_I_Still_Do"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Clapton,_Old_Sock_and_I_Still_Do"><i>Clapton</i>, <i>Old Sock</i> and <i>I Still Do</i></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg/220px-Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg/330px-Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg/440px-Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_in_concert.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton performing in Munich, Germany on 5 June 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>Clapton performed a two-night show with <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">Jeff Beck</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="The O2 Arena (London)">London\'s O2 Arena</a> on <span class="nowrap">13\xe2\x80\x9314 February</span> 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The two former Yardbirds extended their 2010 tour with stops at Madison Square Garden,<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Air_Canada_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Canada Centre">Air Canada Centre</a> in Toronto, and the <a href="/wiki/Bell_Centre" title="Bell Centre">Bell Centre</a> in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Clapton performed a series of concerts in 11 cities throughout the United States from <span class="nowrap">25 February</span> to <span class="nowrap">13 March</span> 2010, including <a href="/wiki/Roger_Daltrey" title="Roger Daltrey">Roger Daltrey</a> as opening act. His third European tour with <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a> began on <span class="nowrap">18 May</span> and ended <span class="nowrap">13 June</span>, including <a href="/wiki/Tom_Norris_(musician)" title="Tom Norris (musician)">Tom Norris</a> as opening act. He then began a short North American tour lasting from <span class="nowrap">26 June</span> to <span class="nowrap">3 July</span>, starting with his third Crossroads Guitar Festival on <span class="nowrap">26 June</span> at <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Park_(Bridgeview)" class="mw-redirect" title="Toyota Park (Bridgeview)">Toyota Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bridgeview,_Illinois" title="Bridgeview, Illinois">Bridgeview, Illinois</a>. Clapton released a new studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Clapton_(2010_album)" title="Clapton (2010 album)">Clapton</a></i>, on <span class="nowrap">27 September</span> 2010 in the United Kingdom and 28 September 2010 in the United States. On <span class="nowrap">17 November</span> 2010, Clapton performed as guest on the <a href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince&#39;s Trust">Prince\'s Trust</a> rock gala held at the Royal Albert Hall, supported by the house band for the evening, which included <a href="/wiki/Jools_Holland" title="Jools Holland">Jools Holland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Midge_Ure" title="Midge Ure">Midge Ure</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mark_King_(musician)" title="Mark King (musician)">Mark King</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton,_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg/220px-Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg/330px-Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg/440px-Eric_Clapton%2C_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton,_Keb_Mo_and_Buddy_Guy_26Jun2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton, <a href="/wiki/Keb%27_Mo%27" title="Keb&#39; Mo&#39;">Keb\' Mo\'</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a> on 26 June 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>On 24 June 2011, Clapton was in concert with <a href="/wiki/Pino_Daniele" title="Pino Daniele">Pino Daniele</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cava_de%27_Tirreni" title="Cava de&#39; Tirreni">Cava de\' Tirreni</a> stadium before performing a series of concerts in South America from 6 to 16 October 2011. He spent November and December 2011 touring Japan with <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a>, playing 13 shows in various cities throughout the country. On 24 February 2012 Clapton, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Richards" title="Keith Richards">Keith Richards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Clark_Jr." title="Gary Clark Jr.">Gary Clark Jr.</a>, Derek Trucks, <a href="/wiki/Doyle_Bramhall_II" title="Doyle Bramhall II">Doyle Bramhall II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Wilson" title="Kim Wilson">Kim Wilson</a> and other artists performed together in the Howlin\' For Hubert Tribute concert held at the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Theater" title="Apollo Theater">Apollo Theater</a> of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> honouring blues guitarist <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Sumlin" title="Hubert Sumlin">Hubert Sumlin</a> who died at age 80 on 4 December 2011. On 29 November 2012, Clapton joined <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a> at London\'s O2 Arena during the band\'s second of five arena dates celebrating their 50th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> On 12 December, Clapton performed <a href="/wiki/12-12-12:_The_Concert_for_Sandy_Relief" title="12-12-12: The Concert for Sandy Relief">The Concert for Sandy Relief</a> at Madison Square Garden, broadcast live via television, radio, cinemas and the Internet across six continents.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In January 2013, Surfdog Records announced a signed deal with Clapton for the release of his forthcoming album <i><a href="/wiki/Old_Sock" title="Old Sock">Old Sock</a></i> on 12 March. On 8 April 2013, Eric and Hard Rock International launched the limited-edition Eric Clapton Artist Spotlight merchandise programme benefiting Crossroads Centre Antigua.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Clapton toured the US and Europe from 14 March to 19 June 2013 to celebrate 50 years as a professional musician.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On 28 February 2013, Clapton announced his intention to stop touring in 2015 due to hassles with travel.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ECPrague2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ECPrague2013.jpg/220px-ECPrague2013.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/ECPrague2013.jpg/330px-ECPrague2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/20/ECPrague2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="431" data-file-height="287" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ECPrague2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton in Prague, June 2013, during his 50th Celebration World Tour</div></div></div>\n<p>On 15 October 2013, Clapton\'s popular <i><a href="/wiki/Unplugged_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Unplugged (Eric Clapton album)">Unplugged</a></i> album and concert DVD were re-released, titled <i>Unplugged: Expanded &amp; Remastered.</i>  The album includes the original 14 tracks, remastered, as well as 6 additional tracks, including 2 versions of "<a href="/wiki/My_Father%27s_Eyes_(song)" title="My Father&#39;s Eyes (song)">My Father\'s Eyes</a>". The DVD includes a restored version of the concert, as well as over 60 minutes of unseen footage from the rehearsal. On 13 and 14 November 2013, Clapton headlined the final two evenings of the "Baloise Sessions", an annual indoor music festival in <a href="/wiki/Basel" title="Basel">Basel</a>, Switzerland. On 20 November 2013, Warner Bros released <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a> 2013 in CD/DVD/Blu-ray. On 30 April 2014, Clapton announced the release of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Breeze:_An_Appreciation_of_JJ_Cale" title="The Breeze: An Appreciation of JJ Cale">The Breeze: An Appreciation of JJ Cale</a></i> as an homage to <a href="/wiki/J._J._Cale" title="J. J. Cale">J. J. Cale</a> who died on 26 July 2013. This tribute album is named after the 1972 single "<a href="/wiki/Call_Me_the_Breeze" title="Call Me the Breeze">Call Me the Breeze</a>" and features 16 Cale songs performed by Clapton, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a>, John Mayer, <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">Willie Nelson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Petty" title="Tom Petty">Tom Petty</a> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 June 2014, Clapton abruptly walked off stage during a concert at the <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Hydro" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Hydro">Glasgow Hydro</a>. Although he did return to perform one final song, thousands of fans were upset by the lack of explanation from Clapton or the venue and booed after the concert ended around 40 minutes before advertised to finish. Both Clapton and the venue apologised the next day, blaming \'technical difficulties\' for making sound conditions \'unbearable\' for Clapton on stage.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> A week later he confirmed his retirement plans attributing his decision to the road being "unbearable" in addition to "odd ailments" that may force him to put down his guitar permanently.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> In a 2016 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Classic_Rock_(magazine)" title="Classic Rock (magazine)">Classic Rock</a></i> magazine, Clapton  revealed that he had been diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Peripheral_neuropathy" title="Peripheral neuropathy">peripheral neuropathy</a> in 2013, a condition which refers to damage in one\'s peripheral nerves and often results in stabbing, burning or tingling pain in the arms and legs.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton performed two shows at <a href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden" title="Madison Square Garden">Madison Square Garden</a> in New York on 1 and 3 May 2015 followed by a 7-night residency at London\'s <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a> from 14 to 23 May 2015 to celebrate his 70th birthday on 30 March.<sup id="cite_ref-Royal_Albert_Hall_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Royal_Albert_Hall-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The shows also mark 50 years since Clapton first played at the Royal Albert Hall \xe2\x80\x93 his debut was on 7 December 1964 when he performed as part of <a href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds" title="The Yardbirds">The Yardbirds</a> for the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s  <i>Top Beat Show</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Royal_Albert_Hall_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Royal_Albert_Hall-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The concert film, <i><a href="/wiki/Slowhand_at_70_%E2%80%93_Live_at_the_Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Slowhand at 70 \xe2\x80\x93 Live at the Royal Albert Hall">Slowhand at 70 \xe2\x80\x93 Live at the Royal Albert Hall</a></i>, was released by <a href="/wiki/Eagle_Rock_Entertainment" title="Eagle Rock Entertainment">Eagle Rock Entertainment</a> on 13 November 2015 on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a>, <a href="/wiki/CD" class="mw-redirect" title="CD">CD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blu-Ray" class="mw-redirect" title="Blu-Ray">Blu-Ray</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammophone_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammophone record">LP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The 2-night concerts in the US marked the 46th anniversary since Clapton, with Cream, opened the "new" Madison Square Garden on 2 November 1968. Clapton has performed more times at Madison Square Garden than any other US venue, a total of 45 times.<sup id="cite_ref-MSG_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MSG-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> On 20 May 2016, Clapton released his twenty-third studio album <i><a href="/wiki/I_Still_Do" title="I Still Do">I Still Do</a></i>. On 30 September 2016 the live-album <i><a href="/wiki/Live_in_San_Diego_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Live in San Diego (Eric Clapton album)">Live in San Diego</a></i> was released.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In August 2018, Clapton announced that he had recorded his twenty-fourth studio album, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Happy_Xmas_(Eric_Clapton_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Happy Xmas (Eric Clapton album) (page does not exist)">Happy Xmas</a></i>, which consists of blues-tinged interpretations of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_music" title="Christmas music">Christmas songs</a> and is scheduled to be released on 12 October.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span></h2>\n<p>Clapton cites <a href="/wiki/Muddy_Waters" title="Muddy Waters">Muddy Waters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freddie_King" title="Freddie King">Freddie King</a>, <a href="/wiki/B.B._King" title="B.B. King">B.B. King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_King" title="Albert King">Albert King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Sumlin" title="Hubert Sumlin">Hubert Sumlin</a> as guitar playing influences.  Clapton stated blues musician <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson_(musician)" class="mw-redirect" title="Robert Johnson (musician)">Robert Johnson</a> to be his single most important influence. In 2004 Clapton released CDs and DVDs entitled <i><a href="/wiki/Me_and_Mr._Johnson#Sessions_for_Robert_J" title="Me and Mr. Johnson">Sessions for Robert Johnson</a></i>, featuring covers of Robert Johnson songs using electric and acoustic guitars.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton co-authored with others the book <i>Discovering Robert Johnson</i>, in which Clapton said Johnson was:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p>...the most important blues musician who ever lived. He was true, absolutely, to his own vision, and as deep as I have gotten into the music over the last 30 years, I have never found anything more deeply soulful than Robert Johnson. His music remains the most powerful cry that I think you can find in the human voice, really. ... it seemed to echo something I had always felt.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<p>Clapton also singled out <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a> as an influence. <i>The Chirping Crickets</i> was the first album Clapton ever bought; he later saw Holly on <i><a href="/wiki/Tonight_at_the_London_Palladium" title="Tonight at the London Palladium">Sunday Night at the London Palladium</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holly_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holly-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> In his autobiography, Clapton recounted the first time he saw Holly and his Fender, saying, "I thought I\'d died and gone to heaven&#160;... it was like seeing an instrument from outer space and I said to myself: \'That\'s the future \xe2\x80\x93 that\'s what I want<span style="padding-right:.2em;">\'</span>".<sup id="cite_ref-Holly_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holly-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Yardbirds_(1998)_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_(2014_photograph).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg/220px-The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg" width="220" height="70" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg/330px-The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg/440px-The_Yardbirds_%281998%29_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_%282014_photograph%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="307" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Yardbirds_(1998)_-_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_handprints_(2014_photograph).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton\'s handprints (far right) with other members of the Yardbirds at the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Clapton has been referred to as one of the most important and influential guitarists of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-AST_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AST-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Meisel_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Meisel-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Clapton is the only <a href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_inductees#Multiple_inductees" title="List of Rock and Roll Hall of Fame inductees">three-time inductee</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame" title="Rock and Roll Hall of Fame">Rock and Roll Hall of Fame</a>: once as a solo artist, and separately as a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Yardbirds" title="The Yardbirds">the Yardbirds</a> and Cream.<sup id="cite_ref-Rock_Hall_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rock_Hall-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> He ranked second in <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine\'s list of the "100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time"<sup id="cite_ref-RS_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and fourth in <i><a href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibson Guitar Corporation">Gibson\'s</a></i> Top 50 Guitarists of All Time.<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> attributed the creation of the cult of the guitar hero to Clapton, ranking it number seven on their list of the 50 key events in rock music history;\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Nothing is more central to rock mythology than the cult of the lead guitarist. And no one did more to create that cult than Eric Clapton. He had already been a member of the Yardbirds before joining John Mayall\'s Bluesbreakers, the clearing house for guitarists, in April 1965. His two stints with Mayall saw his reputation grow to the extent that a famous graffito captured the popular appraisal of him among rock fans: <a href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music" title="Honorific nicknames in popular music">"Clapton is God"</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<p>Guitarists influenced by Clapton include <a href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)" title="Slash (musician)">Slash</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allen_Collins" title="Allen Collins">Allen Collins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richie_Sambora" title="Richie Sambora">Richie Sambora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Ray_Vaughan" title="Stevie Ray Vaughan">Stevie Ray Vaughan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Moore" title="Gary Moore">Gary Moore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duane_Allman" title="Duane Allman">Duane Allman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derek_Trucks" title="Derek Trucks">Derek Trucks</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-derektrucks_inspiration_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-derektrucks_inspiration-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Van_Halen" title="Eddie Van Halen">Eddie Van Halen</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Kath" title="Terry Kath">Terry Kath</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Iommi" title="Tony Iommi">Tony Iommi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz" title="Lenny Kravitz">Lenny Kravitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Nugent" title="Ted Nugent">Ted Nugent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orianthi" title="Orianthi">Orianthi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vince_Gill" title="Vince Gill">Vince Gill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brad_Paisley" title="Brad Paisley">Brad Paisley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jonny_Buckland" title="Jonny Buckland">Jonny Buckland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Don_Rooney" title="Joe Don Rooney">Joe Don Rooney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Lifeson" title="Alex Lifeson">Alex Lifeson</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Mayer" title="John Mayer">John Mayer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Satriani" title="Joe Satriani">Joe Satriani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Bonamassa" title="Joe Bonamassa">Joe Bonamassa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neal_Schon" title="Neal Schon">Neal Schon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a>.\n</p><p>In 2012, Clapton was among the <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Culture of the United Kingdom">British cultural icons</a> selected by artist Sir <a href="/wiki/Peter_Blake_(artist)" title="Peter Blake (artist)">Peter Blake</a> to appear in a new version of his most famous artwork \xe2\x80\x93 the Beatles\' <i><a href="/wiki/Sgt._Pepper%27s_Lonely_Hearts_Club_Band" title="Sgt. Pepper&#39;s Lonely Hearts Club Band">Sgt. Pepper\'s Lonely Hearts Club Band</a></i> album cover \xe2\x80\x93 to celebrate the British cultural figures of his life that he most admires to mark his 80th birthday.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Guitars">Guitars</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg/170px-Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg" width="170" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg/255px-Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg/340px-Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="730" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric-Clapton_1975.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton on the There\'s One in Every Crowd Tour, with "<a href="/wiki/Blackie_(guitar)" title="Blackie (guitar)">Blackie</a>" on 15 August 1975</div></div></div>\n<p>Clapton\'s choice of electric guitars has been as notable as the man himself; like <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">the Beatles</a> and Jimi Hendrix, Clapton exerted a crucial and widespread influence in popularising particular models of electric guitar.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> With the Yardbirds, Clapton played a Fender Telecaster, a <a href="/wiki/Fender_Jazzmaster" title="Fender Jazzmaster">Fender Jazzmaster</a>, a double-cutaway <a href="/wiki/Gretsch_6120" title="Gretsch 6120">Gretsch 6120</a>, and a 1964 Cherry-Red Gibson ES-335. He became exclusively a Gibson player for a period beginning in mid-1965, when he purchased a used sunburst <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Les_Paul" title="Gibson Les Paul">Gibson Les Paul</a> guitar from a guitar store in London. Clapton commented on the slim profile of the neck, which would indicate it was a 1960 model.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Early during his stint in Cream, Clapton\'s first Les Paul Standard was stolen. He continued to play Les Pauls exclusively with Cream (one bought from <a href="/wiki/Andy_Summers" title="Andy Summers">Andy Summers</a> was almost identical to the stolen guitar)<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> until 1967, when he acquired his most famous guitar in this period, a 1964 <a href="/wiki/Gibson_SG" title="Gibson SG">Gibson SG</a>, dubbed "<a href="/wiki/The_Fool_(guitar)" title="The Fool (guitar)">the Fool</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-GIBS_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GIBS-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Clapton used both the Les Paul and the SG to create his self-described "woman tone".<sup id="cite_ref-Oxman_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxman-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>  He explained in a 1967 interview, "I am playing more smoothly now. I\xe2\x80\x99m developing what I call my \'woman tone.\' It\'s a sweet sound, something like the solo on \'I Feel Free\'."<sup id="cite_ref-Oxman_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxman-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>  Writer Michael Dregni describes it as "thick yet piercing, overdriven yet smooth, distorted yet creamy".<sup id="cite_ref-Dregni_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dregni-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>  The tone is achieved by a combination of tone control settings on the guitars and Clapton\'s <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Amplifiers" class="mw-redirect" title="Marshall Amplifiers">Marshall</a> JTM45 amplifier.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>  <i><a href="/wiki/Vintage_Guitar_(magazine)" title="Vintage Guitar (magazine)">Vintage Guitar</a></i> magazine identifies "the opening riff and solo of \'Sunshine of Your Love\' are arguably the best illustrations of full-blown woman tone".<sup id="cite_ref-Oxman_137-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxman-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>  Clapton\'s "Fool" acquired its name from its distinctive psychedelic paint job, created by the visual art collective also known as <a href="/wiki/The_Fool_(design_collective)" title="The Fool (design collective)">the Fool</a> (just before Cream\'s first US appearance in 1967, <a href="/wiki/Gibson_SG#Unique_SGs" title="Gibson SG">Clapton\'s SG</a>, Bruce\'s <a href="/wiki/Fender_VI" class="mw-redirect" title="Fender VI">Fender VI</a>, and Baker\'s drum head were all repainted in psychedelic designs).\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg/170px-Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg/255px-Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg/340px-Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg 2x" data-file-width="683" data-file-height="1024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_1978.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton with Blackie while on tour in the Netherlands, 1978. Clapton recorded hits such as "Cocaine", "I Shot the Sheriff", "Wonderful Tonight", "Farther Up the Road" and "Lay Down Sally" on Blackie</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1968 Clapton bought a <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Firebird" title="Gibson Firebird">Gibson Firebird</a> and started using the 1964 Cherry-Red Gibson ES-335 again.<sup id="cite_ref-GIBS_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GIBS-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The aforementioned 1964 ES-335 had a storied career. Clapton used it at the last Cream show in November 1968 as well as with Blind Faith, played it sparingly for slide pieces in the 1970s, used it on "Hard Times" from <i><a href="/wiki/Journeyman_(album)" title="Journeyman (album)">Journeyman</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Live_in_Hyde_Park_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Live in Hyde Park (Eric Clapton album)">Hyde Park</a> live concert of 1996, and the <i><a href="/wiki/From_the_Cradle" title="From the Cradle">From the Cradle</a></i> sessions and tour of 1994\xe2\x80\x9395. It was sold for US$847,500 at a 2004 auction.<sup id="cite_ref-cdqimo_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdqimo-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Gibson produced a limited run of 250 "Crossroads 335" replicas. The 335 was only the second electric guitar Clapton bought.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 1968 Clapton gave George Harrison a 1957 \'goldtop\' Gibson Les Paul that been refinished with a red colour, nicknamed <a href="/wiki/Lucy_(guitar)" title="Lucy (guitar)">Lucy</a>. The following September, Clapton played the guitar on the Beatles\' recording of "<a href="/wiki/While_My_Guitar_Gently_Weeps" title="While My Guitar Gently Weeps">While My Guitar Gently Weeps</a>". Lucy was stolen from Harrison, though later tracked down and returned to him - he lent it to Clapton for his 1973 comeback <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton%27s_Rainbow_Concert" title="Eric Clapton&#39;s Rainbow Concert">concert at the Rainbow</a>. His SG "The Fool" found its way into the hands of George Harrison\'s friend <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Lomax" title="Jackie Lomax">Jackie Lomax</a>, who subsequently sold it to musician <a href="/wiki/Todd_Rundgren" title="Todd Rundgren">Todd Rundgren</a> for US$500 in 1972. Rundgren restored the guitar and nicknamed it "Sunny", after "Sunshine of Your Love". He retained it until 2000, when he sold it at an auction for US$150,000.<sup id="cite_ref-GIBS_136-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GIBS-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> At the 1969 Blind Faith concert in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park, London</a> Clapton played a <a href="/wiki/Fender_Musical_Instruments_Corporation" title="Fender Musical Instruments Corporation">Fender</a> Custom <a href="/wiki/Telecaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Telecaster">Telecaster</a>, which was fitted with "<a href="/wiki/Brownie_(guitar)" title="Brownie (guitar)">Brownie</a>"<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s neck.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG/220px-Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG/330px-Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG/440px-Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hard_Rock_Cafe_London_Clapton%27s_guitar_Fender.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton\'s Lead II Fender, the first ever piece of memorabilia donated to the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe" title="Hard Rock Cafe">Hard Rock Cafe</a>, London in 1979</div></div></div>\n<p>In late 1969 Clapton made the switch to the <a href="/wiki/Fender_Stratocaster" title="Fender Stratocaster">Fender Stratocaster</a>. "I had a lot of influences when I took up the Strat. First there was <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Holly" title="Buddy Holly">Buddy Holly</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Guy" title="Buddy Guy">Buddy Guy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a> was the first well known person over here in England who was using one, but that wasn\'t really my kind of music. <a href="/wiki/Steve_Winwood" title="Steve Winwood">Steve Winwood</a> had so much credibility, and when he started playing one, I thought, oh, if he can do it, I can do it".<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The first\xe2\x80\x94used during the recording of <i><a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_(album)" title="Eric Clapton (album)">Eric Clapton</a></i>\xe2\x80\x94was "Brownie", which in 1973 became the backup to the most famous of all Clapton\'s guitars, "<a href="/wiki/Blackie_(guitar)" title="Blackie (guitar)">Blackie</a>". In November 1970 Eric bought six Fender Stratocasters from the Sho-bud guitar shop in <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">Nashville, Tennessee</a> while on tour with the Dominos. He gave one each to George Harrison, Steve Winwood, and Pete Townshend.\n</p><p>Clapton assembled the best components of the remaining three to create "Blackie", which was his favourite stage guitar until its retirement in 1985. It was first played live <span class="nowrap">13 January</span> 1973 at the <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton%27s_Rainbow_Concert" title="Eric Clapton&#39;s Rainbow Concert">Rainbow Concert</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Clapton called the 1956/57 Strat a "mongrel".<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On <span class="nowrap">24 June</span> 2004, Clapton sold "Blackie" at <a href="/wiki/Christie%27s" title="Christie&#39;s">Christie\'s</a> Auction House, New York, for US$959,500 to raise funds for his <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre" title="Crossroads Centre">Crossroads Centre</a> for drug and alcohol addictions.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> "Brownie" is now on display at the <a href="/wiki/Experience_Music_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Experience Music Project">Experience Music Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Fender_Custom_Shop" title="Fender Custom Shop">Fender Custom Shop</a> has since produced a limited run of 275 \'Blackie\' replicas, correct in every detail right down to the \'Duck Brothers\' flight case, and artificially aged using Fender\'s \'Relic\' process to simulate years of hard wear. One was presented to Clapton upon the model\'s release and was used for three numbers during a concert at the Royal Albert Hall on <span class="nowrap">17 May</span> 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> In 1979 Clapton gave his signed Fender Lead II guitar to the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Cafe" title="Hard Rock Cafe">Hard Rock Cafe</a> in London to designate his favourite bar stool. Pete Townshend also donated his own Gibson Les Paul guitar, with a note attached: "Mine\'s as good as his! Love, Pete".<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eric_Clapton_1.jpg/220px-Eric_Clapton_1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eric_Clapton_1.jpg/330px-Eric_Clapton_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Eric_Clapton_1.jpg/440px-Eric_Clapton_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4272" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eric_Clapton_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton playing an <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_Stratocaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Clapton Stratocaster">Eric Clapton Stratocaster</a> at the Hard Rock Calling concert in Hyde Park, London in 2008</div></div></div>\n<p>Signature guitars in Clapton\'s honour are made by Fender and <a href="/wiki/C.F._Martin_%26_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="C.F. Martin &amp; Company">C.F. Martin &amp; Company</a>. In 1988 Fender introduction his signature <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_Stratocaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Eric Clapton Stratocaster">Eric Clapton Stratocaster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Several signature-model 000-sized acoustic guitars made by Martin. The first, of these, introduced in 1995, was a limited edition 000-42EC Eric Clapton signature model with a production run of 461. For the single "<a href="/wiki/Change_the_World" title="Change the World">Change the World</a>" (1996) and the album <i><a href="/wiki/Pilgrim_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Pilgrim (Eric Clapton album)">Pilgrim</a></i> (1998) he used a Martin 000-28 EC Eric Clapton signature model, which he subsequently gave to guitarist <a href="/wiki/Paul_Wassif" title="Paul Wassif">Paul Wassif</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bonhams_Auction_Clapton_Guitar_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bonhams_Auction_Clapton_Guitar-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> His 1939 000-42 Martin that he played on the <i>Unplugged</i> album sold for US$791,500 at auction.<sup id="cite_ref-cdqimo_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdqimo-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1999, Clapton auctioned off some of his guitar collection to raise more than US$5 million for continuing support of the Crossroads Centre in Antigua, which he founded in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> In 2004 Clapton organised and participated in the Crossroads Guitar Festival to benefit the centre. A second guitar auction, including the "Cream" of Clapton\'s collection \xe2\x80\x93 as well as guitars donated by famous friends \xe2\x80\x93 was held on <span class="nowrap">24 June</span> 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/George_Lowden" title="George Lowden">Lowden</a> acoustic guitar sold for US$41,825. The revenue garnered by this auction at Christie\'s was US$7,438,624.<sup id="cite_ref-cdqimo_140-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cdqimo-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010 Eric Clapton announced that he would be auctioning off over 150 items at a New York auction in 2011 with proceeds to go to his Crossroads Centre drug and rehabilitation centre in Antigua. Items included Clapton\'s guitar from the Cream reunion tour in 2005, speaker cabinets used in the early 1970s from his days with Derek and the Dominos, and some guitars from Jeff Beck, J. J. Cale, and Joe Bonamassa.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> In March 2011 Clapton raised more than US$2.15 million when he auctioned off key items, including a 1984 Gibson <a href="/wiki/Semi-acoustic_guitar" title="Semi-acoustic guitar">hollow body guitar</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Gianni_Versace" title="Gianni Versace">Gianni Versace</a> suit from his 1990 concert at the Royal Albert Hall, and a replica of the famous Fender Stratocaster known as "Blackie", which fetched more than $30,000. All proceeds again went to Crossroads. Clapton uses <a href="/wiki/Ernie_Ball" title="Ernie Ball">Ernie Ball</a> Slinky and Super Slinky strings, gauge .10 to.46.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> His guitar technician for over thirty years was Lee Dickson.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_media_appearances">Other media appearances</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg/200px-EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg" width="200" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg/300px-EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg/400px-EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="614" data-file-height="627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EricClaptonRockWalkHollywood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clapton\'s handprints in <a href="/wiki/Hollywood,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="Hollywood, California">Hollywood, California</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Clapton frequently appears as a guest on the albums of other musicians. He played lead guitar and synthesiser on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Pros_and_Cons_of_Hitch_Hiking" title="The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking">The Pros and Cons of Hitch Hiking</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a>\' debut solo album. Other media appearances include the <a href="/wiki/Toots_%26_the_Maytals" class="mw-redirect" title="Toots &amp; the Maytals">Toots &amp; the Maytals</a> Grammy award-winning<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> album <i><a href="/wiki/True_Love_(Toots_%26_the_Maytals_album)" title="True Love (Toots &amp; the Maytals album)">True Love</a></i>, where he played guitar on the track "<a href="/wiki/Pressure_Drop_(song)" title="Pressure Drop (song)">Pressure Drop</a>". He played on <a href="/wiki/Paul_Brady" title="Paul Brady">Paul Brady</a>\'s 1985 album <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Centre" title="Back to the Centre">Back to the Centre</a></i> on the track "Deep in your Heart". He can also be heard at the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Frank_Zappa" title="Frank Zappa">Frank Zappa</a>\'s album, <i><a href="/wiki/We%27re_Only_in_It_for_the_Money" title="We&#39;re Only in It for the Money">We\'re Only in It for the Money</a></i>, repeating the phrase, "Are you hung up?" over and over again. In 1985, Clapton appeared on the charity concert <a href="/wiki/Live_Aid" title="Live Aid">Live Aid</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a> with Phil Collins, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Renwick" title="Tim Renwick">Tim Renwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Stainton" title="Chris Stainton">Chris Stainton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Oldaker" title="Jamie Oldaker">Jamie Oldaker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcy_Levy" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcy Levy">Marcy Levy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Murphy_(singer)" title="Shaun Murphy (singer)">Shaun Murphy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Donald_%27Duck%27_Dunn" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald &#39;Duck&#39; Dunn">Donald \'Duck\' Dunn</a>. In 1988 he played with <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_70th_Birthday_Tribute" title="Nelson Mandela 70th Birthday Tribute">Nelson Mandela 70th Birthday Tribute</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Prince%27s_Trust" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince&#39;s Trust">Prince\'s Trust</a> rock gala at the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Albert_Hall" title="Royal Albert Hall">Royal Albert Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> On <span class="nowrap">30 June</span> 1990, Dire Straits, Clapton and Elton John made a guest appearance in the <a href="/wiki/Nordoff-Robbins" class="mw-redirect" title="Nordoff-Robbins">Nordoff-Robbins</a> charity show held at <a href="/wiki/Concerts_at_Knebworth_House" title="Concerts at Knebworth House">Knebworth</a> in England.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> In 1991 Clapton was featured on <a href="/wiki/Richie_Sambora" title="Richie Sambora">Richie Sambora</a>\'s album, <i><a href="/wiki/Stranger_in_This_Town" title="Stranger in This Town">Stranger in This Town</a></i>, in a song dedicated to him, called "Mr. Bluesman".  He contributed guitar and vocals to "Runaway Train", a duet with Elton John on the latter\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_One_(Elton_John_album)" title="The One (Elton John album)">The One</a></i> album the following year.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 12 September 1996 Clapton played a party for <a href="/wiki/Armani" title="Armani">Armani</a> at New York City\'s Lexington Armory with <a href="/wiki/Greg_Phillinganes" title="Greg Phillinganes">Greg Phillinganes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nathan_East" title="Nathan East">Nathan East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Gadd" title="Steve Gadd">Steve Gadd</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sheryl_Crow" title="Sheryl Crow">Sheryl Crow</a> appeared on one number, performing "<a href="/wiki/Tearing_Us_Apart" title="Tearing Us Apart">Tearing Us Apart</a>", a track from <i>August</i>, which was first performed by <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> during the Prince\'s Trust All-Star Rock show in 1986. It was Clapton\'s sole US appearance that year, following the <a href="/wiki/Live_in_Hyde_Park_(Eric_Clapton_album)" title="Live in Hyde Park (Eric Clapton album)">open-air concert</a> held at Hyde Park.<sup id="cite_ref-Hyde_Park_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyde_Park-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The concert was taped and the footage was released both on VHS video cassette and later, on DVD.<sup id="cite_ref-Hyde_Park_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hyde_Park-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton was featured in the movie version of <i>Tommy</i>, the first full length <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a>, written by the Who. The movie version gave Clapton a <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo appearance</a> as the Preacher, performing <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Boy_Williamson_II" title="Sonny Boy Williamson II">Sonny Boy Williamson\'s</a> song, "Eyesight to the Blind". He appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Blues_Brothers_2000" title="Blues Brothers 2000">Blues Brothers 2000</a></i> as one of the Louisiana Gator Boys. In addition to being in the band, he had a small speaking role. Clapton has appeared in an advertisement for the <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_G-Class" title="Mercedes-Benz G-Class">Mercedes-Benz G-Wagen</a>. In March 2007 Clapton appeared in an advertisement<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> for <a href="/wiki/RealNetworks" title="RealNetworks">RealNetwork\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Rhapsody_(online_music_service)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhapsody (online music service)">Rhapsody online music service</a>. In 2010 Clapton started appearing as a spokesman for <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a>, advertising their <a href="/wiki/HTC_Magic" title="HTC Magic">MyTouch</a> Fender cell phone. Clapton also appeared in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> documentary <i>Reggae Got Soul: The Story of <a href="/wiki/Toots_and_the_Maytals" title="Toots and the Maytals">Toots and the Maytals</a></i> which was described as "The untold story of one of the most influential artists ever to come out of Jamaica."<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When asked to describe God by their minister, the characters <a href="/wiki/Eric_Forman" title="Eric Forman">Eric Forman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Hyde" title="Steven Hyde">Steven Hyde</a> both drew an image of Clapton in the episode "<a href="/wiki/Holy_Crap!" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Crap!">Holy Crap!</a>" of season two of <i><a href="/wiki/That_%2770s_Show" title="That &#39;70s Show">That \'70s Show</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Clapton appeared on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">Top Gear</a></i> in 2013, during Series 19 Episode 4 and was involved in testing the new <a href="/wiki/Kia_Cee%27d" class="mw-redirect" title="Kia Cee&#39;d">Kia Cee\'d</a>. He was called upon to test the Cee\'d\'s auxiliary input, which he tested by plugging in one of his guitars and playing several bars of his most famous hits. He was introduced by <i>Top Gear</i> host <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Clarkson" title="Jeremy Clarkson">Jeremy Clarkson</a> as a "local guitarist".<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017, a documentary film titled <i>Eric Clapton: Life in 12 Bars</i> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Lili_Fini_Zanuck" title="Lili Fini Zanuck">Lili Fini Zanuck</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>  Clapton wrote the film score for Zanuck\'s 1991 film <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_(1991_film)" title="Rush (1991 film)">Rush</a></i> and the two remained friends.<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>  In an interview for <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a>, Zanuck said that Clapton only agreed to participate if she directed it:\n</p>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303468"/><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>"I think this got made because Eric was in the right mood. He\'s an incredibly private man and despite his immense success, he\'s never cared if he got any publicity at all, he just loves his music<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... I think it might be something to do with his age, as he turned 70 a couple of years ago. He said to me, "I didn\'t want it to be done after I was dead and for it to be wrong." Maybe he thought his time had come to lay it all out on the table.<span style="padding-right:.2em;">\'</span>"<sup id="cite_ref-Jones_163-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships_and_children">Relationships and children</span></h3>\n<p>Clapton and <a href="/wiki/Pattie_Boyd" title="Pattie Boyd">Pattie Boyd</a> married in 1979, but had no children. In 1984 while recording <i>Behind The Sun</i>, Clapton began a relationship with Yvonne Kelly, the manager of <a href="/wiki/Associated_Independent_Recording" title="Associated Independent Recording">AIR Studios Montserrat</a>. Although both were married to other partners at the time, they had a daughter in January 1985. She was named Ruth Kelly Clapton, but her existence was kept from the public until the media realised she was his child in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton and Boyd tried unsuccessfully to have children, even trying <a href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilisation" title="In vitro fertilisation">in vitro fertilisation</a> in 1984, but were faced instead with miscarriages.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> They divorced in 1988 following his affair with Italian model <a href="/wiki/Lory_Del_Santo" title="Lory Del Santo">Lory Del Santo</a>, who gave birth to their son, Conor, on <span class="nowrap">21 August</span> 1986. Conor died in 1991 at the age of 4 1/2 after falling out of an open bedroom window on the 53rd floor of a Manhattan apartment building.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton married Melia McEnery in a low-key church ceremony in January 2002.
