They have three daughters: Julie Rose (born June 13, 2001), Ella May (born January 14, 2003) and Sophie Belle (born February 1, 2005).<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> His grandson Isaac Eric Owen Bartlett was born in June 2013 to his oldest daughter Ruth and her husband Dean Bartlett.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_views">Political views</span></h3>\n<p>Clapton is a supporter of the <a href="/wiki/Countryside_Alliance" title="Countryside Alliance">Countryside Alliance</a> which promotes issues relating to the British countryside. He has played in concerts to raise funds for the organisation and publicly opposed the <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour Party</a>\'s ban on <a href="/wiki/Fox_hunting" title="Fox hunting">fox hunting</a> with the 2004 <a href="/wiki/Hunting_Act_2004" title="Hunting Act 2004">Hunting Act</a>. A spokesperson for Clapton said, "Eric supports the Countryside Alliance. He doesn\'t hunt himself, but does enjoy rural pursuits such as fishing and shooting. He supports the Alliance\'s pursuit to scrap the ban on the basis that he doesn\'t agree with the state\'s interference with people\'s private pursuits".<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy_over_remarks_on_immigration">Controversy over remarks on immigration</span></h3>\n<p>On 5 August 1976, Clapton provoked an uproar and lingering controversy when he spoke out against increasing immigration during a concert in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>. Visibly intoxicated, Clapton voiced his support of controversial political candidate <a href="/wiki/Enoch_Powell" title="Enoch Powell">Enoch Powell</a>, and announced on stage that Britain was in danger of becoming a "black colony". Among other things, Clapton said "Keep Britain white!"<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> which was at the time a <a href="/wiki/British_National_Front" class="mw-redirect" title="British National Front">National Front</a> (NF) slogan.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> This incident, along with some controversial remarks made around the same time by <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-TW_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TW-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> as well as uses of <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a>-related imagery by <a href="/wiki/Sid_Vicious" title="Sid Vicious">Sid Vicious</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siouxsie_Sioux" title="Siouxsie Sioux">Siouxsie Sioux</a>, were the main catalysts for the creation of <a href="/wiki/Rock_Against_Racism" title="Rock Against Racism">Rock Against Racism</a>, with a concert on 30 April 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-racism_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-racism-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In an interview from October 1976 with <i><a href="/wiki/Sounds_(magazine)" title="Sounds (magazine)">Sounds</a></i> magazine, Clapton said that he was not a political person and that his rambling remarks that night were not appropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-Farther_On_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Farther_On-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In a 2004 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Uncut_(magazine)" title="Uncut (magazine)">Uncut</a></i>, Clapton referred to Powell as "outrageously brave".<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> He complained that the UK was "... inviting people in as cheap labour and then putting them in ghettos."<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, Clapton told an interviewer for <i><a href="/wiki/Scotland_on_Sunday" title="Scotland on Sunday">Scotland on Sunday</a></i>, "There\'s no way I could be a racist. It would make no sense."<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In his 2007 autobiography, Clapton claimed to be "oblivious to it all".<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> In a December 2007 interview with <a href="/wiki/Melvyn_Bragg" title="Melvyn Bragg">Melvyn Bragg</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/The_South_Bank_Show" title="The South Bank Show">The South Bank Show</a></i>, Clapton told Bragg that he wasn\'t a racist but still believed Powell\'s comments were relevant.<sup id="cite_ref-TW_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TW-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wealth_and_assets">Wealth and assets</span></h3>\n<p>In 2009, <i>Surrey Life Magazine</i> ranked Clapton as number 17 in their list of richest <a href="/wiki/Surrey" title="Surrey">Surrey</a> residents, estimating his fortune at \xc2\xa3120 million in assets. This was a combination of property and income which include a \xc2\xa39 million <a href="/wiki/Yacht" title="Yacht">yacht</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Va_Bene_(yacht)" title="Va Bene (yacht)">Va Bene</a></i> (previously owned by <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Ecclestone" title="Bernie Ecclestone">Bernie Ecclestone</a>), his back <a href="/wiki/Music_catalogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Music catalogue">music catalogue</a>, his touring income, and his <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> Marshbrook Ltd, which had earned him \xc2\xa3110 million since 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-Clapton&#39;s_estimated_wealth_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clapton&#39;s_estimated_wealth-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> In 2003, he purchased a 50% share of gentleman\'s outfitters Cordings Piccadilly.<sup id="cite_ref-Clapton_rescues_gentlemen&#39;s_shop_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clapton_rescues_gentlemen&#39;s_shop-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> At the time, owner Noll Uloth was trying to save the shop from closure and is reported to have contacted Clapton, his "best client"; within five minutes, Clapton replied with "I can\'t let this happen".<sup id="cite_ref-Clapton_rescues_gentlemen&#39;s_shop_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clapton_rescues_gentlemen&#39;s_shop-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Car_collection">Car collection</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FerrariSP12EC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FerrariSP12EC.jpg/220px-FerrariSP12EC.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FerrariSP12EC.jpg/330px-FerrariSP12EC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FerrariSP12EC.jpg/440px-FerrariSP12EC.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FerrariSP12EC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ferrari_SP12_EC" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrari SP12 EC">Ferrari SP12 EC</a> built for Clapton under Ferrari\'s Special Projects programme<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Since the 1970s, Clapton considered himself a "car enthusiast" and often stated his passion for the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari" title="Ferrari">Ferrari</a> brand.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Clapton currently owns or has owned a range of Ferraris, and when asked about his Ferrari collection in 1989, he said he liked the touring cars for road use the company produces and commented "if I had more space and if I had been wise I would have a huge collection by now and I would be a multi-multi-millionaire".<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, he explained that for him "Ferrari has always been the number one car" to own and drive, and that he always supported Ferrari on the road and in <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> motor racing.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, Ferrari honoured Clapton with the one-off special project car, the <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_SP12_EC" class="mw-redirect" title="Ferrari SP12 EC">Ferrari SP12 EC</a>. In July 2013 Clapton displayed it at the <a href="/wiki/Goodwood_Festival_of_Speed" title="Goodwood Festival of Speed">Goodwood Festival of Speed</a> in England in the Michelin Supercar Run.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Clapton explained that Ferrari is still his favourite car brand.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> Among the other vehicles Clapton owns or has owned during his life are a vintage <a href="/wiki/Mini" title="Mini">Mini Cooper Radford</a> which was a gift from George Harrison.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_work">Charitable work</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_Fender_Stratocaster_Eric_Clapton_Signature_Model,_Serial_No._CN98950_(Bonhams_auction_19226,_lot_136)_%26_2005_Gibson_ES-335_Crossroads_Model_Prototype,_Serial_No._Prototype_3_(lot_116).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/2005_Fender_Stratocaster_Eric_Clapton_Signature_Model%2C_Serial_No._CN98950_%28Bonhams_auction_19226%2C_lot_136%29_%26_2005_Gibson_ES-335_Crossroads_Model_Prototype%2C_Serial_No._Prototype_3_%28lot_116%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/2005_Fender_Stratocaster_Eric_Clapton_Signature_Model%2C_Serial_No._CN98950_%28Bonhams_auction_19226%2C_lot_136%29_%26_2005_Gibson_ES-335_Crossroads_Model_Prototype%2C_Serial_No._Prototype_3_%28lot_116%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/2005_Fender_Stratocaster_Eric_Clapton_Signature_Model%2C_Serial_No._CN98950_%28Bonhams_auction_19226%2C_lot_136%29_%26_2005_Gibson_ES-335_Crossroads_Model_Prototype%2C_Serial_No._Prototype_3_%28lot_116%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2005_Fender_Stratocaster_Eric_Clapton_Signature_Model,_Serial_No._CN98950_(Bonhams_auction_19226,_lot_136)_%26_2005_Gibson_ES-335_Crossroads_Model_Prototype,_Serial_No._Prototype_3_(lot_116).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Auction of Clapton\'s guitars and amps in aid of the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre" title="Crossroads Centre">Crossroads Centre</a></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1993, Clapton was appointed a director of <a href="/wiki/Clouds_House" title="Clouds House">Clouds House</a>, a UK treatment centre for drug and alcohol dependence, and served on their board until 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Clapton also served on the board of directors for The Chemical Dependency Centre from 1994 until 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Both charities subsequently merged to become <a href="/wiki/Action_on_Addiction" title="Action on Addiction">Action on Addiction</a> in 2007.\n</p><p>In 1998, he established the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Centre" title="Crossroads Centre">Crossroads Centre</a> in Antigua to help others overcome their addictions to drugs and alcohol and is active in its management oversight and fundraising to the present day.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Clapton has organised the <a href="/wiki/Crossroads_Guitar_Festival" title="Crossroads Guitar Festival">Crossroads Guitar Festival</a> in 1999, 2004, 2007, 2010 and 2013 to raise funds for this centre.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Clapton has collaborated with <a href="/wiki/The_Prince%27s_Trust" title="The Prince&#39;s Trust">The Prince\'s Trust</a>, the leading UK youth charity which provides training, personal development, business start up support, mentoring, and advice. He has performed at the charity\'s rock concert numerous times since the 1980s, most recently in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2008, he donated a song to <a href="/wiki/Aid_Still_Required" title="Aid Still Required">Aid Still Required</a>\'s CD to assist with the restoration of the devastation done to Southeast Asia from the <a href="/wiki/2004_tsunami" class="mw-redirect" title="2004 tsunami">2004 tsunami</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span></h3>\n<p>Clapton is a fan of English <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> football club <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-West_Brom_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_Brom-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In 1982 he performed a concert before West Brom player <a href="/wiki/John_Wile" title="John Wile">John Wile</a>\'s testimonial game at <a href="/wiki/The_Hawthorns" title="The Hawthorns">The Hawthorns</a>. It has been reported that the club rejected his offer to invest cash in the club around this time. In the late 1970s Clapton positioned a West Brom scarf on the back cover of his album, <i>Backless</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> In the 1978-79 season Clapton sponsored West Brom\'s <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> home game against Turkish club <a href="/wiki/Galatasaray_S.K." title="Galatasaray S.K.">Galatasaray</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-West_Brom_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-West_Brom-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="width:95%;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th align="center">Year\n</th>\n<th>Award / Recognition\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>1983</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Presented the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Clef_Award" title="Silver Clef Award">Silver Clef Award</a> from <a href="/wiki/Princess_Michael_of_Kent" title="Princess Michael of Kent">Princess Michael of Kent</a> for outstanding contribution to British music.<sup id="cite_ref-crossroads_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossroads-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>1985</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Presented with <a href="/wiki/BAFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a> for Best Original Television Music for Score of <i><a href="/wiki/Edge_of_Darkness" title="Edge of Darkness">Edge of Darkness</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kamen" title="Michael Kamen">Michael Kamen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>1993</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>"Tears in Heaven" won three Grammy awards for Song of the Year, Record of the Year, and Male Pop Vocal Performance. Clapton also won Album of the Year and Best Rock Vocal Performance for <i>Unplugged</i> and Best Rock Song for "Layla".<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>1995</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Made an <a href="/wiki/Officer_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Officer of the Order of the British Empire">Officer of the Order of the British Empire</a> (OBE) for services to music, as part of the 1995 New Year Honours list.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>2000</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Inducted into the Rock and Roll Hall of Fame for the third time, this time as a solo artist. He was earlier inducted as a member of the bands Cream and the Yardbirds.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>2004</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Promoted to <a href="/wiki/Commander_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander of the Order of the British Empire">Commander of the Order of the British Empire</a> (CBE), receiving the award from the <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Royal</a> at Buckingham Palace as part of the 2004 New Year Honours list.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>2006</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Awarded the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a> as a member of Cream.<sup id="cite_ref-Lifetime_Achievement_Award1_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lifetime_Achievement_Award1-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>2015</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>An asteroid, <a href="/wiki/4305_Clapton" class="mw-redirect" title="4305 Clapton">4305 Clapton</a>, is named after him.\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center"><b>2017</b>\n</td>\n<td>\n<p>Made a <i>Commandeur</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Ordre_des_Arts_et_des_Lettres" title="Ordre des Arts et des Lettres">Ordre des Arts et des Lettres</a> of France<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span id="Clapton.27s_music_in_film_and_TV"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Clapton\'s_music_in_film_and_TV">Clapton\'s music in film and TV</span></h2>\n<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50" /></div></div></td>\n<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">\n<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Change_The_World_sample.ogg" class="mw-redirect" title="File:Change The World sample.ogg">"Change the World"</a></div>\n<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" soundtrack.</div></div></td></tr>\n<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Clapton\'s music has appeared in dozens of movies and television shows as far back as 1973\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Mean_Streets" title="Mean Streets">Mean Streets</a></i> which featured the song "I Looked Away". Other appearances in media include in the <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_Vice" title="Miami Vice">Miami Vice</a></i> series ("<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_Tonight" title="Wonderful Tonight">Wonderful Tonight</a>", "Knock on Wood", "She\'s Waiting", and "<a href="/wiki/Layla" title="Layla">Layla</a>"), <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Future" title="Back to the Future">Back to the Future</a></i> ("Heaven Is One Step Away"), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Color_of_Money" title="The Color of Money">The Color of Money</a></i> ("It\'s In The Way That You Use It"), <i><a href="/wiki/Lethal_Weapon_2" title="Lethal Weapon 2">Lethal Weapon 2</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Knockin%27_On_Heaven%27s_Door" class="mw-redirect" title="Knockin&#39; On Heaven&#39;s Door">Knockin\' On Heaven\'s Door</a>"), <i><a href="/wiki/Goodfellas" title="Goodfellas">Goodfellas</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Layla" title="Layla">Layla</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Sunshine_of_Your_Love" title="Sunshine of Your Love">Sunshine of Your Love</a>"),<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Freaks_and_Geeks" title="Freaks and Geeks">Freaks and Geeks</a></i> episode "I\'m With the Band" ("<a href="/wiki/Sunshine_of_Your_Love" title="Sunshine of Your Love">Sunshine of Your Love</a>", "<a href="/wiki/White_Room" title="White Room">White Room</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Crossroads_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Crossroads (song)">Crossroads (song)</a>"), <i><a href="/wiki/Friends" title="Friends">Friends</a></i> episodes "<a href="/wiki/The_One_with_the_Proposal,_Part_2" class="mw-redirect" title="The One with the Proposal, Part 2">The One with the Proposal, Part 2</a>" ("<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_Tonight" title="Wonderful Tonight">Wonderful Tonight</a>") and "The One Where Rachel Has A Baby" ("River of Tears"), <i><a href="/wiki/School_Of_Rock" class="mw-redirect" title="School Of Rock">School Of Rock</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Sunshine_Of_Your_Love" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunshine Of Your Love">Sunshine Of Your Love</a>)", <i><a href="/wiki/Men_in_Black_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Men in Black III">Men in Black III</a></i> ("Strange Brew"), <i><a href="/wiki/Captain_Phillips_(film)" title="Captain Phillips (film)">Captain Phillips (film)</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_Tonight" title="Wonderful Tonight">Wonderful Tonight</a>"), <i><a href="/wiki/August:_Osage_County_(film)" title="August: Osage County (film)">August: Osage County (film)</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Lay_Down_Sally" title="Lay Down Sally">Lay Down Sally</a>") for which it was a significant part of the soundtrack, being played in the intro and twice more later on, <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Girls_Revolt" title="Good Girls Revolt">Good Girls Revolt</a></i> episode "The Year-Ender" ("<a href="/wiki/White_Room" title="White Room">White Room</a>)" and <i><a href="/wiki/Rick_and_Morty" title="Rick and Morty">Rick and Morty</a></i> episode "Summer\'s Future" ("It\'s In The Way That You Use It").<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Both <a href="/wiki/Opel" title="Opel">Opel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vauxhall_Motors" title="Vauxhall Motors">Vauxhall</a> used the guitar riff from "<a href="/wiki/Layla" title="Layla">Layla</a>" in their advertising campaigns throughout 1987\xe2\x80\x9395.  In addition to his music appearing in media, Clapton has contributed to several movies by writing or co-writing the musical scores or contributing original songs. These movies include <i><a href="/wiki/Lethal_Weapon" title="Lethal Weapon">Lethal Weapon</a></i> (co-written with Michael Kamen),<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Communion_(1989_film)" title="Communion (1989 film)">Communion</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rush_(1991_film)" title="Rush (1991 film)">Rush</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Phenomenon_(film)" title="Phenomenon (film)">Phenomenon</a></i> ("<a href="/wiki/Change_the_World" title="Change the World">Change the World</a>"), and <i><a href="/wiki/Lethal_Weapon_3" title="Lethal Weapon 3">Lethal Weapon 3</a></i> (co-wrote and co-performed "It\'s Probably Me" with <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> and "Runaway Train" with Elton John).<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Eric_Clapton_discography" title="Eric Clapton discography">Eric
